<a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States"><img alt="President of the United States" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Seal_of_the_President_of_the_United_States.svg/40px-Seal_of_the_President_of_the_United_States.svg.png" width="40" height="40" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Seal_of_the_President_of_the_United_States.svg/60px-Seal_of_the_President_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Seal_of_the_President_of_the_United_States.svg/80px-Seal_of_the_President_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="2424" data-file-height="2425" /></a></p>
<div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini">
<ul>
<li class="nv-view"><b><a href="/wiki/Template:BillClintonseries" title="Template:BillClintonseries"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></b></li>
<li class="nv-talk"><b><a href="/w/index.php?title=Template_talk:BillClintonseries&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Template talk:BillClintonseries (page does not exist)"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></b></li>
<li class="nv-edit"><b><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:BillClintonseries&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></b></li>
</ul>

</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p><b>William Jefferson Clinton</b> (August 19, 1946), born <span class="nowrap"><b>William Jefferson Blythe III</b>,</span> is an <a href="/wiki/Americans" title="Americans">American</a> politician who served as the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Presidents_of_the_United_States" title="List of Presidents of the United States">42nd</a> <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">President of the United States</a> from 1993 to 2001. He previously served as <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Arkansas" title="Governor of Arkansas" class="mw-redirect">Governor of Arkansas</a> from 1979 to 1981 and 1983 to 1992, and as the <a href="/wiki/Arkansas_Attorney_General" title="Arkansas Attorney General">state's Attorney General</a> from 1977 to 1979. A member of the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democratic Party</a>, ideologically Clinton was a <a href="/wiki/New_Democrats" title="New Democrats">New Democrat</a>, and many of his policies reflected a <a href="/wiki/Centrism" title="Centrism">centrist</a> the <a href="/wiki/Third_Way" title="Third Way">Third Way</a> philosophy of governance.</p>
<p>Clinton was born and raised in <a href="/wiki/Arkansas" title="Arkansas">Arkansas</a>, and is an alumnus of <a href="/wiki/Georgetown_University" title="Georgetown University">Georgetown University</a>, where he was a member of <a href="/wiki/Kappa_Kappa_Psi" title="Kappa Kappa Psi">Kappa Kappa Psi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Phi_Beta_Kappa" title="Phi Beta Kappa" class="mw-redirect">Phi Beta Kappa</a> and earned a <a href="/wiki/Rhodes_Scholarship" title="Rhodes Scholarship">Rhodes Scholarship</a> to attend the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Oxford" title="University of Oxford">University of Oxford</a>. He is married to <a href="/wiki/Hillary_Clinton" title="Hillary Clinton">Hillary Clinton</a>, who served as <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_State" title="United States Secretary of State">United States Secretary of State</a> from 2009 to 2013 and who was a <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_Senators_from_New_York" title="List of United States Senators from New York">Senator from New York</a> from 2001 to 2009. Both Clintons earned <a href="/wiki/Juris_Doctor" title="Juris Doctor">law degrees</a> from <a href="/wiki/Yale_Law_School" title="Yale Law School">Yale Law School</a>, where they met and began dating. As <a href="/wiki/List_of_Governors_of_Arkansas" title="List of Governors of Arkansas">Governor of Arkansas</a>, Clinton overhauled the state's education system, and served as <a href="/wiki/Chair" title="Chair">Chair</a> of the <a href="/wiki/National_Governors_Association" title="National Governors Association">National Governors Association</a>.</p>
<p>Clinton was elected president in <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_1992" title="United States presidential election, 1992">1992</a>, defeating incumbent <a href="/wiki/George_H._W._Bush" title="George H. W. Bush">George H. W. Bush</a>. Aged 46, he was the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Presidents_of_the_United_States_by_age" title="List of Presidents of the United States by age">third-youngest president</a> and the first from the <a href="/wiki/Baby_boomer" title="Baby boomer" class="mw-redirect">baby boomer</a> generation. Clinton presided over the longest period of peacetime economic expansion in American history, and signed into law the <a href="/wiki/North_American_Free_Trade_Agreement" title="North American Free Trade Agreement">North American Free Trade Agreement</a>. After failing to pass <a href="/wiki/Clinton_health_care_plan" title="Clinton health care plan" class="mw-redirect">national health care reform</a>, the Democratic House was ousted when the <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">Republican Party</a> <a href="/wiki/Republican_Revolution" title="Republican Revolution">won control</a> of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Congress" title="United States Congress">Congress</a> in 1994 for the first time in 40 years. Two years later, Clinton became the first Democrat since <a href="/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt" title="Franklin D. Roosevelt">Franklin D. Roosevelt</a> to be elected president twice. He passed <a href="/wiki/Welfare_reform" title="Welfare reform">welfare reform</a> and the <a href="/wiki/State_Children%27s_Health_Insurance_Program" title="State Children's Health Insurance Program">State Children's Health Insurance Program</a>, providing health coverage for millions of children. In 1998, he was <a href="/wiki/Impeachment_of_Bill_Clinton" title="Impeachment of Bill Clinton" class="mw-redirect">impeached</a> for <a href="/wiki/Perjury" title="Perjury">perjury</a> before a <a href="/wiki/Grand_jury" title="Grand jury">grand jury</a> and <a href="/wiki/Obstruction_of_justice" title="Obstruction of justice">obstruction of justice</a> during a lawsuit against him, both related to a <a href="/wiki/Lewinsky_scandal" title="Lewinsky scandal">scandal</a> involving White House (and later <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Defense" title="United States Department of Defense">Department of Defense</a>) employee <a href="/wiki/Monica_Lewinsky" title="Monica Lewinsky">Monica Lewinsky</a>. He was acquitted by the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Senate" title="U.S. Senate" class="mw-redirect">U.S. Senate</a> and served his complete term of office. The <a href="/wiki/Congressional_Budget_Office" title="Congressional Budget Office">Congressional Budget Office</a> reported a budget surplus between the years 1998 and 2000, the last three years of Clinton's presidency.</p>
<p>Clinton left office with the highest end-of-office <a href="/wiki/Approval_rating" title="Approval rating" class="mw-redirect">approval rating</a> of any U.S. president since <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>. Since then, he has been involved in public speaking and humanitarian work. Clinton created the <a href="/wiki/Clinton_Foundation" title="Clinton Foundation">William J. Clinton Foundation</a> to address international causes such as the prevention of AIDS and <a href="/wiki/Global_warming" title="Global warming">global warming</a>. In 2004, he published his autobiography <i><a href="/wiki/My_Life_(Bill_Clinton_autobiography)" title="My Life (Bill Clinton autobiography)">My Life</a></i>. He has remained active in politics by campaigning for Democratic candidates, most notably for <a href="/wiki/Hillary_Clinton_presidential_campaign,_2008" title="Hillary Clinton presidential campaign, 2008">his wife's campaign for the 2008 Democratic presidential nomination</a>, and then <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a>'s presidential campaigns in <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama_presidential_campaign,_2008" title="Barack Obama presidential campaign, 2008">2008</a> and <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama_presidential_campaign,_2012" title="Barack Obama presidential campaign, 2012">2012</a>. In 2009, he was named United Nations <a href="/wiki/Special_Envoy_of_the_Secretary-General" title="Special Envoy of the Secretary-General">Special Envoy</a> to <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">Haiti</a>, and after the <a href="/wiki/2010_Haiti_earthquake" title="2010 Haiti earthquake">2010 Haiti earthquake</a> he teamed with <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a> to form the <a href="/wiki/Clinton_Bush_Haiti_Fund" title="Clinton Bush Haiti Fund">Clinton Bush Haiti Fund</a>. Since leaving office, Clinton has been rated highly in <a href="/wiki/Historical_rankings_of_Presidents_of_the_United_States" title="Historical rankings of Presidents of the United States">public opinion polls of U.S. presidents</a>.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life_and_career">Early life and career</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:William_Jefferson_Blythe_1950.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/William_Jefferson_Blythe_1950.jpg/170px-William_Jefferson_Blythe_1950.jpg" width="170" height="269" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/William_Jefferson_Blythe_1950.jpg/255px-William_Jefferson_Blythe_1950.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/William_Jefferson_Blythe_1950.jpg/340px-William_Jefferson_Blythe_1950.jpg 2x" data-file-width="362" data-file-height="573" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:William_Jefferson_Blythe_1950.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
William Jefferson Blythe III, in 1950 at age four</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bill_Clinton_Boyhood_Home_in_Hope,_Arkansas_IMG_1515.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Bill_Clinton_Boyhood_Home_in_Hope%2C_Arkansas_IMG_1515.JPG/170px-Bill_Clinton_Boyhood_Home_in_Hope%2C_Arkansas_IMG_1515.JPG" width="170" height="128" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Bill_Clinton_Boyhood_Home_in_Hope%2C_Arkansas_IMG_1515.JPG/255px-Bill_Clinton_Boyhood_Home_in_Hope%2C_Arkansas_IMG_1515.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Bill_Clinton_Boyhood_Home_in_Hope%2C_Arkansas_IMG_1515.JPG/340px-Bill_Clinton_Boyhood_Home_in_Hope%2C_Arkansas_IMG_1515.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bill_Clinton_Boyhood_Home_in_Hope,_Arkansas_IMG_1515.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Clinton's boyhood home in <a href="/wiki/Hope,_Arkansas" title="Hope, Arkansas">Hope, Arkansas</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Clinton was born William Jefferson Blythe III on August 19, 1946, at Julia Chester Hospital in <a href="/wiki/Hope,_Arkansas" title="Hope, Arkansas">Hope, Arkansas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-My_Life_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-My_Life-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> His father, <a href="/wiki/William_Jefferson_Blythe,_Jr." title="William Jefferson Blythe, Jr.">William Jefferson Blythe, Jr.</a> (1918–1946), was a traveling salesman who died in an automobile accident three months before Clinton was born.<sup id="cite_ref-whitehouse.gov_bio_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-whitehouse.gov_bio-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup> His mother, <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Clinton_Kelley" title="Virginia Clinton Kelley">Virginia Dell</a> (née Cassidy; 1923–1994), traveled to <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans" title="New Orleans">New Orleans</a> to study nursing soon after he was born. She left Clinton in Hope with her parents Eldridge and Edith Cassidy, who owned and ran a small <a href="/wiki/Grocery_store" title="Grocery store">grocery store</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-My_Life_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-My_Life-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> At a time when the Southern United States was <a href="/wiki/Racial_segregation_in_the_United_States" title="Racial segregation in the United States">segregated racially</a>, Clinton's grandparents sold goods on <a href="/wiki/Credit_(finance)" title="Credit (finance)">credit</a> to people of all races.<sup id="cite_ref-My_Life_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-My_Life-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1950, Bill's mother returned from nursing school and married <a href="/wiki/Roger_Clinton,_Sr." title="Roger Clinton, Sr.">Roger Clinton, Sr.</a>, who owned an <a href="/wiki/Car_dealership" title="Car dealership">automobile dealership</a> in <a href="/wiki/Hot_Springs,_Arkansas" title="Hot Springs, Arkansas">Hot Springs, Arkansas</a>, with his brother and <a href="/wiki/Earl_T._Ricks" title="Earl T. Ricks">Earl T. Ricks</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-My_Life_3-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-My_Life-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> The family moved to Hot Springs in 1950.</p>
<p>Although he immediately assumed use of his stepfather's surname, it was not until Clinton turned fifteen<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> that he formally adopted the surname Clinton as a gesture toward his stepfather.<sup id="cite_ref-My_Life_3-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-My_Life-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> Clinton says he remembers his stepfather as a <a href="/wiki/Gambler" title="Gambler" class="mw-redirect">gambler</a> and an alcoholic who regularly <a href="/wiki/Domestic_violence" title="Domestic violence">abused</a> his mother and half-brother, <a href="/wiki/Roger_Clinton,_Jr." title="Roger Clinton, Jr.">Roger Clinton, Jr.</a>, to the point where he intervened multiple times with the threat of violence to protect them.<sup id="cite_ref-My_Life_3-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-My_Life-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-First_In_His_Class_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-First_In_His_Class-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In Hot Springs, Clinton attended St. John's Catholic Elementary School, <a href="/wiki/Primary_school" title="Primary school">Ramble Elementary School</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hot_Springs_High_School_(Arkansas)" title="Hot Springs High School (Arkansas)">Hot Springs High School</a>&#160;– where he was an active student leader, avid reader, and musician.<sup id="cite_ref-My_Life_3-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-My_Life-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> Clinton was in the chorus and played the <a href="/wiki/Tenor_saxophone" title="Tenor saxophone">tenor saxophone</a>, winning first chair in the state band's saxophone section. He briefly considered dedicating his life to music, but as he noted in his autobiography <i><a href="/wiki/My_Life_(Bill_Clinton_autobiography)" title="My Life (Bill Clinton autobiography)">My Life</a></i>:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>Sometime in my sixteenth year, I decided I wanted to be in public life as an elected official. I loved music and thought I could be very good, but I knew I would never be <a href="/wiki/John_Coltrane" title="John Coltrane">John Coltrane</a> or <a href="/wiki/Stan_Getz" title="Stan Getz">Stan Getz</a>. I was interested in medicine and thought I could be a fine doctor, but I knew I would never be <a href="/wiki/Michael_E._DeBakey" title="Michael E. DeBakey">Michael DeBakey</a>. But I knew I could be great in public service.<sup id="cite_ref-My_Life_3-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-My_Life-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>Clinton's interest in law also began in Hot Springs High, when in his Latin class he took up the challenge to argue the defense of the ancient <a href="/wiki/Roman_Senator" title="Roman Senator" class="mw-redirect">Roman Senator</a> <a href="/wiki/Catiline" title="Catiline">Catiline</a> in a mock trial.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> After a vigorous defense that made use of his "budding rhetorical and political skills", he told the Latin teacher Elizabeth Buck that it "made him realize that someday he would study law."<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Clinton has named two influential moments in his life that contributed to his decision to become a public figure, both occurring in 1963. One was his visit as a <a href="/wiki/Boys_Nation" title="Boys Nation">Boys Nation</a> senator to the <a href="/wiki/White_House" title="White House">White House</a> to meet President <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy" title="John F. Kennedy">John F. Kennedy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-My_Life_3-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-My_Life-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-First_In_His_Class_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-First_In_His_Class-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> The other was listening to <a href="/wiki/Martin_Luther_King,_Jr." title="Martin Luther King, Jr.">Martin Luther King, Jr.</a>'s 1963 <i><a href="/wiki/I_Have_a_Dream" title="I Have a Dream">I Have a Dream</a></i> speech, which impressed him enough that he later memorized it.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="College_and_law_school_years">College and law school years</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Georgetown_University">Georgetown University</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Clinton_at_Georgetown_1967.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Clinton_at_Georgetown_1967.jpg/220px-Clinton_at_Georgetown_1967.jpg" width="220" height="282" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Clinton_at_Georgetown_1967.jpg/330px-Clinton_at_Georgetown_1967.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Clinton_at_Georgetown_1967.jpg/440px-Clinton_at_Georgetown_1967.jpg 2x" data-file-width="690" data-file-height="884" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Clinton_at_Georgetown_1967.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Clinton ran for President of the <a href="/wiki/Georgetown_University_Student_Association" title="Georgetown University Student Association">Student Council</a> while attending the School of Foreign Service at <a href="/wiki/Georgetown_University" title="Georgetown University">Georgetown University</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>With the aid of scholarships, Clinton attended the <a href="/wiki/Edmund_A._Walsh_School_of_Foreign_Service" title="Edmund A. Walsh School of Foreign Service">Edmund A. Walsh School of Foreign Service</a> at <a href="/wiki/Georgetown_University" title="Georgetown University">Georgetown University</a> in Washington, D.C., receiving a <a href="/wiki/List_of_tagged_degrees" title="List of tagged degrees">Bachelor of Science in Foreign Service</a> (B.S.) degree in 1968. In 1964 and 1965 he won elections for <a href="/wiki/Class_president" title="Class president">class president</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> From 1964 to 1967 he was an intern and then a clerk in the office of Arkansas Senator <a href="/wiki/J._William_Fulbright" title="J. William Fulbright">J. William Fulbright</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-My_Life_3-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-My_Life-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> While in college, he became a brother of co-ed service fraternity <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Phi_Omega" title="Alpha Phi Omega">Alpha Phi Omega</a><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> and was elected to <a href="/wiki/Phi_Beta_Kappa" title="Phi Beta Kappa" class="mw-redirect">Phi Beta Kappa</a>. Clinton was also a member of the Order of <a href="/wiki/DeMolay_International" title="DeMolay International">DeMolay</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> a youth group affiliated with Freemasonry, but he never became a <a href="/wiki/Freemasonry" title="Freemasonry">Freemason</a>. He is a member of <a href="/wiki/Kappa_Kappa_Psi" title="Kappa Kappa Psi">Kappa Kappa Psi</a> honorary band fraternity.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rhodes_Scholar">Rhodes Scholar</span></h3>
<p>Upon graduation, he won a <a href="/wiki/Rhodes_Scholarship" title="Rhodes Scholarship">Rhodes Scholarship</a> to <a href="/wiki/University_College,_Oxford" title="University College, Oxford">University College, Oxford</a> where he studied <a href="/wiki/Philosophy,_Politics_and_Economics" title="Philosophy, Politics and Economics" class="mw-redirect">Philosophy, Politics and Economics</a>, though because he had switched programs and had left early for Yale University, he did not receive a degree there.<sup id="cite_ref-First_In_His_Class_6-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-First_In_His_Class-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> He developed an interest in <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">rugby union</a>, playing at Oxford<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> and later for the Little Rock Rugby club in Arkansas.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Vietnam_War_opposition_and_draft_controversy">Vietnam War opposition and draft controversy</span></h3>
<p>While at Oxford he also participated in <a href="/wiki/Opposition_to_the_Vietnam_War" title="Opposition to the Vietnam War" class="mw-redirect">Vietnam War protests</a> and organized an October 1969 <a href="/wiki/Moratorium_to_End_the_War_in_Vietnam" title="Moratorium to End the War in Vietnam">Moratorium to End the War in Vietnam</a> event.<sup id="cite_ref-My_Life_3-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-My_Life-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Clinton received <a href="/wiki/Vietnam_War" title="Vietnam War">Vietnam War</a> draft deferments during 1968 and 1969 while he was in England.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> Planning to attend law school in the U.S, and aware that he might lose his draft deferment, he tried unsuccessfully to obtain positions in the <a href="/wiki/National_Guard_of_the_United_States" title="National Guard of the United States">National Guard</a> or <a href="/wiki/United_States_Air_Force" title="United States Air Force">Air Force</a>, and then made arrangements to join the <a href="/wiki/Reserve_Officers%27_Training_Corps" title="Reserve Officers' Training Corps">Reserve Officers' Training Corps</a> (ROTC) program at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Arkansas" title="University of Arkansas">University of Arkansas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>He subsequently decided not to join the ROTC, saying in a letter to the officer in charge of the program he had planned to join that he opposed the war, but did not think it was honorable to use ROTC, National Guard, or Reserve service to avoid serving in Vietnam. He further stated that because he opposed the war, he would not volunteer to serve in uniform, but would subject himself to the draft, and would serve if selected only as a way "to maintain my political viability within the system."<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup> Clinton registered for the draft and received a high number (311), meaning that those whose birthdays had been drawn as numbers 1 to 310 would have to be drafted before him, which was unlikely. Clinton's political opponents charge that he used Fulbright's influence to avoid military service.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Colonel_(United_States)" title="Colonel (United States)">Colonel</a> Eugene Holmes, the Army officer who had been involved with Clinton's ROTC application, suspected that Clinton attempted to manipulate the situation to avoid the draft and avoid serving in uniform. He issued a <a href="/wiki/Notarize" title="Notarize" class="mw-redirect">notarized</a> statement during the 1992 presidential campaign:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>I was informed by the draft board that it was of interest to Senator Fulbright's office that Bill Clinton, a Rhodes Scholar, should be admitted to the <a href="/wiki/ROTC" title="ROTC" class="mw-redirect">ROTC</a> program&#160;… I believe that he purposely deceived me, using the possibility of joining the ROTC as a ploy to work with the draft board to delay his induction and get a new draft classification.<sup id="cite_ref-Morris1999_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Morris1999-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>During the 1992 campaign it was revealed that Clinton's uncle had attempted to secure him a position in the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy_Reserve" title="United States Navy Reserve">Navy Reserve</a>, which would have kept him from going to Vietnam. This effort was unsuccessful and Clinton said in 1992 that he had been unaware of it until then.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> Although legal, Clinton's actions with respect to the draft and deciding whether to serve in the military were criticized by conservatives and some Vietnam veterans during his first presidential campaign.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> Clinton's 1992 campaign manager, <a href="/wiki/James_Carville" title="James Carville">James Carville</a>, successfully argued that Clinton's letter in which he declined to join the ROTC should be made public, insisting that voters, many of whom had also opposed the Vietnam War, would understand and appreciate his position.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Law_school">Law school</span></h3>
<p>After Oxford, Clinton attended <a href="/wiki/Yale_Law_School" title="Yale Law School">Yale Law School</a> and earned a <a href="/wiki/Juris_Doctor" title="Juris Doctor">Juris Doctor</a> (J.D.) degree in 1973.<sup id="cite_ref-My_Life_3-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-My_Life-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-First_In_His_Class_6-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-First_In_His_Class-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/Lillian_Goldman_Law_Library" title="Lillian Goldman Law Library">Yale Law Library</a> in 1971 he met fellow law student <a href="/wiki/Hillary_Clinton" title="Hillary Clinton">Hillary Rodham</a>, who was a year ahead of him.<sup id="cite_ref-My_Life_3-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-My_Life-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-HRCBio_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HRCBio-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup> They began dating and soon were inseparable. After only about a month, Clinton postponed his plans to be a coordinator for the <a href="/wiki/George_McGovern_presidential_campaign,_1972" title="George McGovern presidential campaign, 1972">George McGovern campaign</a> for the <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_1972" title="United States presidential election, 1972">1972 United States presidential election</a> in order to move in with her in California.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> They married on October 11, 1975, and their only child, <a href="/wiki/Chelsea_Clinton" title="Chelsea Clinton">Chelsea</a>, was born on February 27, 1980.<sup id="cite_ref-HRCBio_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HRCBio-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Clinton did eventually move to Texas with Rodham to take a job leading <a href="/wiki/George_McGovern" title="George McGovern">George McGovern</a>'s effort there in 1972. He spent considerable time in <a href="/wiki/Dallas" title="Dallas">Dallas</a>, at the campaign's local headquarters on Lemmon Avenue, where he had an office. Clinton worked with future two-term <a href="/wiki/List_of_mayors_of_Dallas" title="List of mayors of Dallas">mayor of Dallas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ron_Kirk" title="Ron Kirk">Ron Kirk</a>, future <a href="/wiki/List_of_Governors_of_Texas" title="List of Governors of Texas">governor of Texas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ann_Richards" title="Ann Richards">Ann Richards</a>, and then unknown television director (and future filmmaker) <a href="/wiki/Steven_Spielberg" title="Steven Spielberg">Steven Spielberg</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_political_career.2C_1976.E2.80.9392">Early political career, 1976–92</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Electoral_history_of_Bill_Clinton" title="Electoral history of Bill Clinton">Electoral history of Bill Clinton</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Governor_of_Arkansas_.281979.E2.80.9381.2C_1983.E2.80.9392.29">Governor of Arkansas (1979–81, 1983–92)</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Arkansas_gubernatorial_election,_1978" title="Arkansas gubernatorial election, 1978">Arkansas gubernatorial election, 1978</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arkansas_gubernatorial_election,_1980" title="Arkansas gubernatorial election, 1980">Arkansas gubernatorial election, 1980</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arkansas_gubernatorial_election,_1982" title="Arkansas gubernatorial election, 1982">Arkansas gubernatorial election, 1982</a></div>
<p>After graduating from Yale Law School, Clinton returned to Arkansas and became a law professor at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Arkansas" title="University of Arkansas">University of Arkansas</a>. In 1974 he ran for the <a href="/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="United States House of Representatives">House of Representatives</a>. Running in a conservative district against incumbent Republican <a href="/wiki/John_Paul_Hammerschmidt" title="John Paul Hammerschmidt">John Paul Hammerschmidt</a>, Clinton's campaign was bolstered by the anti-Republican and anti-incumbent mood resulting from the <a href="/wiki/Watergate_scandal" title="Watergate scandal">Watergate scandal</a>. Hammerschmidt, who had received 77 percent of the vote in 1972, defeated Clinton by only a 52&#160;percent to 48&#160;percent margin. In 1976 Clinton ran for <a href="/wiki/Arkansas_Attorney_General" title="Arkansas Attorney General">Arkansas Attorney General</a>. With only minor opposition in the primary and no opposition at all in the general election,<sup id="cite_ref-AllPolitics1_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AllPolitics1-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> Clinton was elected.<sup id="cite_ref-First_In_His_Class_6-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-First_In_His_Class-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bill_Clinton_1978.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Bill_Clinton_1978.jpg/220px-Bill_Clinton_1978.jpg" width="220" height="156" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Bill_Clinton_1978.jpg/330px-Bill_Clinton_1978.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Bill_Clinton_1978.jpg/440px-Bill_Clinton_1978.jpg 2x" data-file-width="511" data-file-height="363" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bill_Clinton_1978.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Clinton, as the newly elected <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Arkansas" title="Governor of Arkansas" class="mw-redirect">Governor of Arkansas</a>, meeting with President <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Carter" title="Jimmy Carter">Jimmy Carter</a> in 1978</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Clinton was elected <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Arkansas" title="Governor of Arkansas" class="mw-redirect">Governor of Arkansas</a> in 1978, having defeated the Republican candidate <a href="/wiki/Lynn_Lowe" title="Lynn Lowe">Lynn Lowe</a>, a farmer from <a href="/wiki/Texarkana,_Arkansas" title="Texarkana, Arkansas">Texarkana</a>. He became the youngest governor in the country at 32. Due to his youthful appearance, Clinton was often called the "Boy Governor".<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup> He worked on educational reform and Arkansas's roads, with wife Hillary leading a successful committee on urban health care reform. However, his term included an unpopular motor vehicle tax and citizens' anger over the escape of Cuban refugees (from the <a href="/wiki/Mariel_boatlift" title="Mariel boatlift">Mariel boatlift</a>) detained in <a href="/wiki/Fort_Chaffee" title="Fort Chaffee" class="mw-redirect">Fort Chaffee</a> in 1980. <a href="/wiki/Monroe_Schwarzlose" title="Monroe Schwarzlose">Monroe Schwarzlose</a> of <a href="/wiki/Kingsland,_Arkansas" title="Kingsland, Arkansas">Kingsland</a> in <a href="/wiki/Cleveland_County,_Arkansas" title="Cleveland County, Arkansas">Cleveland County</a>, polled 31&#160;percent of the vote against Clinton in the Democratic gubernatorial primary of 1980. Some suggested Schwarzlose's unexpected voter turnout foreshadowed Clinton's defeat in the general election that year by <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">Republican</a> challenger <a href="/wiki/Frank_D._White" title="Frank D. White">Frank D. White</a>. As Clinton once joked, he was the youngest ex-governor in the nation's history.<sup id="cite_ref-First_In_His_Class_6-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-First_In_His_Class-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Clinton joined friend <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Lindsey" title="Bruce Lindsey">Bruce Lindsey</a>'s Little Rock law firm of Wright, Lindsey and Jennings.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1982, he was again elected governor and kept the office for ten years; beginning with the 1986 election, Arkansas had changed its gubernatorial term of office from two to four years. During his term he helped transform Arkansas's economy and improved the state's educational system.<sup id="cite_ref-pendleton_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pendleton-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup> For <a href="/wiki/Senior_citizens" title="Senior citizens" class="mw-redirect">senior citizens</a>, he removed the <a href="/wiki/Sales_tax" title="Sales tax">sales tax</a> from medications and increased the home property-tax exemption.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Natural_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Natural-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup> He became a leading figure among the <a href="/wiki/New_Democrats" title="New Democrats">New Democrats</a>, a group of <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democrats</a> who advocated welfare reform, smaller government, and other policies not supported by liberals. Formally organized as the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Leadership_Council" title="Democratic Leadership Council">Democratic Leadership Council</a> (DLC), the New Democrats argued that in light of President <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Reagan" title="Ronald Reagan">Ronald Reagan</a>'s <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_1984" title="United States presidential election, 1984">landslide victory in 1984</a>, the Democratic Party needed to adopt a more centrist political stance in order to succeed at the national level.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Natural_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Natural-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup> Clinton delivered the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_response_to_the_State_of_the_Union_address" title="Democratic response to the State of the Union address" class="mw-redirect">Democratic response</a> to President Reagan's <a href="/wiki/1985_State_of_the_Union_Address" title="1985 State of the Union Address">1985 State of the Union Address</a> and served as Chair of the <a href="/wiki/National_Governors_Association" title="National Governors Association">National Governors Association</a> from 1986 to 1987, bringing him to an audience beyond Arkansas.<sup id="cite_ref-First_In_His_Class_6-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-First_In_His_Class-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In the early 1980s, Clinton made reform of the Arkansas education system a top priority. Chaired by Clinton's wife <a href="/wiki/Hillary_Clinton" title="Hillary Clinton">Hillary Rodham Clinton</a>, also an attorney and chair of the <a href="/wiki/Legal_Services_Corporation" title="Legal Services Corporation">Legal Services Corporation</a>, the Arkansas Education Standards Committee transformed Arkansas's education system from the worst in the United States to one of the best. Proposed reforms included more spending for schools (supported by a sales-tax increase), better opportunities for gifted children, vocational education, higher teachers' salaries, more course variety, and compulsory teacher competency exams. The reforms passed in September 1983 after Clinton called a special <a href="/wiki/Arkansas_General_Assembly" title="Arkansas General Assembly">legislative session</a>—the longest in Arkansas history.<sup id="cite_ref-pendleton_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pendleton-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup> Many have considered this the greatest achievement of the Clinton governorship.<sup id="cite_ref-First_In_His_Class_6-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-First_In_His_Class-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-The_Natural_33-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Natural-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup> He defeated four Republican candidates for governor: Lowe (1978), White (1982 and 1986), <a href="/wiki/Jonesboro,_Arkansas" title="Jonesboro, Arkansas">Jonesboro</a> businessmen <a href="/wiki/Woody_Freeman" title="Woody Freeman">Woody Freeman</a> (1984), and <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Nelson" title="Sheffield Nelson">Sheffield Nelson</a> of Little Rock (1990).<sup id="cite_ref-AllPolitics1_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AllPolitics1-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The Clintons' personal and business affairs in the 1980s included transactions that became the basis of the <a href="/wiki/Whitewater_controversy" title="Whitewater controversy">Whitewater controversy</a> investigation that later dogged his presidential administration.<sup id="cite_ref-Clinton_Wars_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Clinton_Wars-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup> After extensive investigation over several years, no indictments were made against the Clintons related to the years in Arkansas.<sup id="cite_ref-First_In_His_Class_6-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-First_In_His_Class-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-The_Survivor_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Survivor-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>According to some sources, Clinton was in his early years a death penalty opponent who switched positions.<sup id="cite_ref-mbsrgd_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mbsrgd-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup> During Clinton's term, Arkansas performed its first executions since 1964 (the death penalty had been re-enacted on March 23, 1973).<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup> As Governor, he oversaw four executions: one by <a href="/wiki/Electric_chair" title="Electric chair">electric chair</a> and three by <a href="/wiki/Lethal_injection" title="Lethal injection">lethal injection</a>. Later, as president, Clinton was the first President to pardon a death-row inmate since the federal death penalty was reintroduced in 1988.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1988_Democratic_presidential_primaries">1988 Democratic presidential primaries</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Reagans_with_the_Clintons.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Reagans_with_the_Clintons.jpg/220px-Reagans_with_the_Clintons.jpg" width="220" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Reagans_with_the_Clintons.jpg/330px-Reagans_with_the_Clintons.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Reagans_with_the_Clintons.jpg/440px-Reagans_with_the_Clintons.jpg 2x" data-file-width="683" data-file-height="450" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Reagans_with_the_Clintons.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Governor and Mrs. Clinton attend the Dinner Honoring the Nation's Governors in the <a href="/wiki/White_House" title="White House">White House</a> with President <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Reagan" title="Ronald Reagan">Ronald Reagan</a> and first lady <a href="/wiki/Nancy_Reagan" title="Nancy Reagan">Nancy Reagan</a>, 1987.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1987, there was media speculation Clinton would enter the race after then-<a href="/wiki/Governor_of_New_York" title="Governor of New York">New York Governor</a> <a href="/wiki/Mario_Cuomo" title="Mario Cuomo">Mario Cuomo</a> declined to run and Democratic front-runner <a href="/wiki/Gary_Hart" title="Gary Hart">Gary Hart</a> withdrew owing to revelations of marital infidelity. Clinton decided to remain as Arkansas governor (following consideration for the potential candidacy of Hillary Rodham Clinton for governor, initially favored&#160;– but ultimately vetoed&#160;– by the First Lady).<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup> For the nomination, Clinton endorsed <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Massachusetts" title="Governor of Massachusetts">Massachusetts Governor</a> <a href="/wiki/Michael_Dukakis" title="Michael Dukakis">Michael Dukakis</a>. He gave the nationally televised opening night address at the <a href="/wiki/1988_Democratic_National_Convention" title="1988 Democratic National Convention">1988 Democratic National Convention</a>, but his speech, which was 33 minutes long and twice as long as it was expected to be, was criticized for being too long<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup> and poorly delivered.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup> Presenting himself as a moderate and a member of the New Democrat wing of the Democratic Party, he headed the moderate <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Leadership_Council" title="Democratic Leadership Council">Democratic Leadership Council</a> in 1990 and 1991.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Natural_33-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Natural-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-The_Choice_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Choice-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Presidency_.281993.E2.80.932001.29">Presidency (1993–2001)</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Presidency_of_Bill_Clinton" title="Presidency of Bill Clinton">Presidency of Bill Clinton</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:US_President_Bill_Clinton_Presidential_Trips.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/US_President_Bill_Clinton_Presidential_Trips.svg/220px-US_President_Bill_Clinton_Presidential_Trips.svg.png" width="220" height="112" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/US_President_Bill_Clinton_Presidential_Trips.svg/330px-US_President_Bill_Clinton_Presidential_Trips.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/US_President_Bill_Clinton_Presidential_Trips.svg/440px-US_President_Bill_Clinton_Presidential_Trips.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="940" data-file-height="477" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:US_President_Bill_Clinton_Presidential_Trips.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Countries visited by President Clinton during his terms in office.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>During his presidency, <a href="/wiki/Presidency_of_Bill_Clinton#Legislation_and_programs" title="Presidency of Bill Clinton">Clinton advocated for a wide variety of legislation and programs</a>, much of which was enacted into law or was implemented by the executive branch. His policies, particularly the <a href="/wiki/North_American_Free_Trade_Agreement" title="North American Free Trade Agreement">North American Free Trade Agreement</a> and <a href="/wiki/Welfare_reform" title="Welfare reform">welfare reform</a>, have been attributed to a <a href="/wiki/Centrism" title="Centrism">centrist</a> <a href="/wiki/Third_Way" title="Third Way">Third Way</a> philosophy of governance.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> On budgetary matters his policy of <a href="/wiki/Fiscal_conservatism" title="Fiscal conservatism">fiscal conservatism</a> helped to reduce deficits.<sup id="cite_ref-wp070914_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wp070914-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bbc010115_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc010115-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup> Clinton presided over the longest period of peacetime economic expansion in American history.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NYTExpansion_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTExpansion-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Congressional_Budget_Office" title="Congressional Budget Office">Congressional Budget Office</a> reported budget surpluses of $69&#160;billion in 1998, $126&#160;billion in 1999, and $236&#160;billion in 2000,<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup> during the last three years of Clinton's presidency.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup> The U.S. treasury reported a debt of $5.413 trillion in 1997, and a debt of $5.656 trillion in 1999.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup> At the end of his presidency, Clinton moved to New York and helped his wife win election to the U.S. Senate there.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1992_presidential_campaign">1992 presidential campaign</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)_presidential_primaries,_1992" title="Democratic Party (United States) presidential primaries, 1992" class="mw-redirect">Democratic Party (United States) presidential primaries, 1992</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_1992" title="United States presidential election, 1992">United States presidential election, 1992</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bill_Clinton_presidential_campaign,_1992" title="Bill Clinton presidential campaign, 1992">Bill Clinton presidential campaign, 1992</a></div>
<p>In the first primary contest, the <a href="/wiki/Iowa_caucus" title="Iowa caucus" class="mw-redirect">Iowa caucus</a>, Clinton finished a distant third to Iowa Senator <a href="/wiki/Tom_Harkin" title="Tom Harkin">Tom Harkin</a>. During the campaign for the <a href="/wiki/New_Hampshire_primary" title="New Hampshire primary">New Hampshire primary</a>, reports of an extramarital affair with <a href="/wiki/Gennifer_Flowers" title="Gennifer Flowers">Gennifer Flowers</a> surfaced. As Clinton fell far behind former <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts" title="Massachusetts">Massachusetts</a> Senator <a href="/wiki/Paul_Tsongas" title="Paul Tsongas">Paul Tsongas</a> in the New Hampshire polls,<sup id="cite_ref-First_In_His_Class_6-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-First_In_His_Class-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> following <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XXVI" title="Super Bowl XXVI">Super Bowl XXVI</a>, Clinton and his wife Hillary went on <i><a href="/wiki/60_Minutes" title="60 Minutes">60 Minutes</a></i> to rebuff the charges. Their television appearance was a calculated risk, but Clinton regained several delegates. He finished second to Tsongas in the <a href="/wiki/New_Hampshire_Democratic_primary,_1992" title="New Hampshire Democratic primary, 1992" class="mw-redirect">New Hampshire primary</a>, but after trailing badly in the polls and coming within single digits of winning, the media viewed it as a victory. News outlets labeled him "The Comeback Kid" for earning a firm second-place finish.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Winning the big prizes of Florida and Texas and many of the <a href="/wiki/Southern_United_States" title="Southern United States">Southern primaries</a> on <a href="/wiki/Super_Tuesday" title="Super Tuesday">Super Tuesday</a> gave Clinton a sizable delegate lead. However, former California Governor <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Brown" title="Jerry Brown">Jerry Brown</a> was scoring victories and Clinton had yet to win a significant contest outside his native South.<sup id="cite_ref-First_In_His_Class_6-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-First_In_His_Class-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-The_Choice_44-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Choice-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup> With no major Southern state remaining, Clinton targeted New York, which had many delegates. He scored a resounding victory in New York City, shedding his image as a regional candidate.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Choice_44-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Choice-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup> Having been transformed into the consensus candidate, he secured the Democratic Party nomination, finishing with a victory in <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Brown" title="Jerry Brown">Jerry Brown</a>'s home state of California.<sup id="cite_ref-First_In_His_Class_6-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-First_In_His_Class-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Clinton_family.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Clinton_family.jpg/170px-Clinton_family.jpg" width="170" height="234" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Clinton_family.jpg/255px-Clinton_family.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Clinton_family.jpg/340px-Clinton_family.jpg 2x" data-file-width="469" data-file-height="645" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Clinton_family.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Clinton family in the <a href="/wiki/White_House" title="White House">White House</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>During the campaign, questions of <a href="/wiki/Conflict_of_interest" title="Conflict of interest">conflict of interest</a> regarding state business and the politically powerful <a href="/wiki/Rose_Law_Firm" title="Rose Law Firm">Rose Law Firm</a>, at which Hillary Rodham Clinton was a partner, arose. Clinton argued the questions were moot because all transactions with the state had been deducted before determining Hillary's firm pay.<sup id="cite_ref-My_Life_3-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-My_Life-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup> Further concern arose when Bill Clinton announced that, with Hillary, voters would be getting two presidents "for the price of one".<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>While campaigning for U.S. President, the then Governor Clinton returned to Arkansas to see that <a href="/wiki/Ricky_Ray_Rector" title="Ricky Ray Rector">Ricky Ray Rector</a> would be executed. After killing a police officer and a civilian, Rector shot himself in the head, leading to what his lawyers said was a state where he could still talk but did not understand the idea of death. According to Arkansas state and Federal law, a seriously mentally impaired inmate cannot be executed. The courts disagreed with the allegation of grave mental impairment and allowed the execution. Clinton's return to Arkansas for the execution was framed in a <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> article as a possible political move to counter "soft on crime" accusations.<sup id="cite_ref-mbsrgd_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mbsrgd-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Because Bush's <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_approval_rating" title="United States presidential approval rating">approval ratings</a> were around 80&#160;percent during the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_War" title="Gulf War">Gulf War</a>, he was described as unbeatable. However, when Bush compromised with Democrats to try to lower Federal deficits, he reneged on his <a href="/wiki/Read_my_lips:_no_new_taxes" title="Read my lips: no new taxes">promise not to raise taxes</a>, hurting his approval rating. Clinton repeatedly condemned Bush for making a promise he failed to keep.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Choice_44-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Choice-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup> By election time, the economy was souring and Bush saw his approval rating plummet to just slightly over 40&#160;percent.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Choice_44-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Choice-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup> Finally, conservatives were previously united by anti-communism, but with the end of the Cold War, the party lacked a uniting issue. When <a href="/wiki/Pat_Buchanan" title="Pat Buchanan">Pat Buchanan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pat_Robertson" title="Pat Robertson">Pat Robertson</a> addressed Christian themes at the <a href="/wiki/1992_Republican_National_Convention" title="1992 Republican National Convention">Republican National Convention</a>&#160;– with Bush criticizing Democrats for omitting God from their platform&#160;– many moderates were alienated.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup> Clinton then pointed to his moderate, "New Democrat" record as governor of Arkansas, though some on the more liberal side of the party remained suspicious.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup> Many Democrats who had supported <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Reagan" title="Ronald Reagan">Ronald Reagan</a> and Bush in previous elections switched their support to Clinton.<sup id="cite_ref-BBConthisday_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBConthisday-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup> Clinton and his running mate, <a href="/wiki/Al_Gore" title="Al Gore">Al Gore</a>, toured the country during the final weeks of the campaign, shoring up support and pledging a "new beginning".<sup id="cite_ref-BBConthisday_62-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBConthisday-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Clinton won the <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_1992" title="United States presidential election, 1992">1992 presidential election</a> (43.0&#160;percent of the vote) against Republican incumbent <a href="/wiki/George_H._W._Bush" title="George H. W. Bush">George H. W. Bush</a> (37.4&#160;percent of the vote) and billionaire <a href="/wiki/Populism" title="Populism">populist</a> <a href="/wiki/Ross_Perot" title="Ross Perot">Ross Perot</a>, who ran as an independent (18.9&#160;percent of the vote) on a platform focusing on domestic issues; a significant part of Clinton's success was Bush's steep decline in public approval.<sup id="cite_ref-BBConthisday_62-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBConthisday-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup> Clinton's election ended twelve years of Republican rule of the <a href="/wiki/White_House" title="White House">White House</a> and twenty of the previous twenty-four years. The election gave Democrats full control of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Congress" title="United States Congress">United States Congress</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-whitehouse.gov_bio_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-whitehouse.gov_bio-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup> the first time one party controlled both the executive and legislative branches since Democrats held the <a href="/wiki/95th_United_States_Congress" title="95th United States Congress">95th United States Congress</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Carter" title="Jimmy Carter">Jimmy Carter</a> presidency in the late 1970s.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="First_term.2C_1993.E2.80.9397">First term, 1993–97</span></h3>
<table class="mbox-small" style="border:1px solid #aaa;background-color:#f9f9f9;">

<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bill_Clinton_taking_the_oath_of_office,_1993.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Bill_Clinton_taking_the_oath_of_office%2C_1993.jpg/220px-Bill_Clinton_taking_the_oath_of_office%2C_1993.jpg" width="220" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Bill_Clinton_taking_the_oath_of_office%2C_1993.jpg/330px-Bill_Clinton_taking_the_oath_of_office%2C_1993.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Bill_Clinton_taking_the_oath_of_office%2C_1993.jpg/440px-Bill_Clinton_taking_the_oath_of_office%2C_1993.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2472" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bill_Clinton_taking_the_oath_of_office,_1993.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Clinton takes the <a href="/wiki/Oath_of_office_of_the_President_of_the_United_States" title="Oath of office of the President of the United States">oath of office</a> from Chief Justice <a href="/wiki/William_Rehnquist" title="William Rehnquist">William Rehnquist</a> during his <a href="/wiki/First_inauguration_of_Bill_Clinton" title="First inauguration of Bill Clinton">1993 presidential inauguration</a> on January 20, 1993.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:103px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Coat_of_Arms_of_Bill_Clinton.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Coat_of_Arms_of_Bill_Clinton.svg/101px-Coat_of_Arms_of_Bill_Clinton.svg.png" width="101" height="140" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Coat_of_Arms_of_Bill_Clinton.svg/152px-Coat_of_Arms_of_Bill_Clinton.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Coat_of_Arms_of_Bill_Clinton.svg/202px-Coat_of_Arms_of_Bill_Clinton.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="395" data-file-height="546" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Coat_of_Arms_of_Bill_Clinton.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Clinton's coat of arms, granted by the <a href="/wiki/Chief_Herald_of_Ireland" title="Chief Herald of Ireland" class="mw-redirect">Chief Herald of Ireland</a> in 1995.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Clinton was <a href="/wiki/First_inauguration_of_Bill_Clinton" title="First inauguration of Bill Clinton">inaugurated</a> as the 42nd President of the United States on January 20, 1993. Shortly after taking office, Clinton signed the <a href="/wiki/Family_and_Medical_Leave_Act_of_1993" title="Family and Medical Leave Act of 1993">Family and Medical Leave Act of 1993</a> on February 5, which required large employers to allow employees to take unpaid leave for pregnancy or a serious medical condition. This action had bipartisan support,<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup> and proved quite popular with the public.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Two days after taking office, on January 22, 1993—the 20th anniversary of the U.S. Supreme Court decision in <i><a href="/wiki/Roe_v._Wade" title="Roe v. Wade">Roe v. Wade</a></i>, Clinton reversed restrictions on domestic and international <a href="/wiki/Family_planning" title="Family planning">family planning</a> programs that had been imposed by Clinton's predecessors, Ronald Regan and George H.W. Bush.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup> Clinton said that abortion should be kept "safe, legal, and rare"—a slogan that had been suggested by University of California, San Diego political scientist <a href="/wiki/Samuel_L._Popkin" title="Samuel L. Popkin">Samuel L. Popkin</a> and first used by Clinton in December 1991, while campaigning.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup> During the eight years of the Clinton administration, the U.S. abortion rate declined by about 18.4 percent.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On February 15, 1993, Clinton made his first address to the nation, announcing his plan to raise taxes to cap the <a href="/wiki/Budget_deficit" title="Budget deficit" class="mw-redirect">budget deficit</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup> Two days later, in a nationally televised address to a <a href="/wiki/Joint_session_of_Congress" title="Joint session of Congress" class="mw-redirect">joint session of Congress</a>, Clinton unveiled his economic plan. The plan focused on reducing the deficit rather than on cutting taxes for the middle class, which had been high on his campaign agenda.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup> Clinton's advisers pressured him to raise taxes on the theory that a smaller federal budget deficit would reduce bond interest rates.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On May 19, 1993, Clinton fired seven employees of the White House Travel Office, causing the <a href="/wiki/White_House_travel_office_controversy" title="White House travel office controversy">White House travel office controversy</a> even though the Travel Office staff served at the pleasure of the president and could be <a href="/wiki/At-will_employment" title="At-will employment">dismissed without cause</a>. The White House responded to the controversy by claiming the firings were done because of financial improprieties that had been revealed by a brief FBI investigation.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup> Critics contended the firings had been done to allow friends of the Clintons to take over the travel business and that the involvement of the FBI was unwarranted.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: left; clear: left; margin: 0.5em 1.4em 0.8em 0; width:30em; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #c6dbf7;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>"Our democracy must be not only the envy of the world but the engine of our own renewal. There is nothing wrong with America that cannot be cured by what is right with America."</p>
</div>
</div>
<div style="text-align: left;"><cite>Inaugural address, January 20, 1993.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup></cite></div>
</div>
<p>Clinton signed the <a href="/wiki/Omnibus_Budget_Reconciliation_Act_of_1993" title="Omnibus Budget Reconciliation Act of 1993">Omnibus Budget Reconciliation Act of 1993</a> in August of that year, which passed Congress without a Republican vote. It cut taxes for fifteen million low-income families, made tax cuts available to 90&#160;percent of small businesses,<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup> and raised taxes on the wealthiest 1.2&#160;percent of taxpayers. Additionally, through the implementation of spending restraints, it mandated the budget be balanced over a number of years.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bill_Clinton,_Yitzhak_Rabin,_Yasser_Arafat_at_the_White_House_1993-09-13.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Bill_Clinton%2C_Yitzhak_Rabin%2C_Yasser_Arafat_at_the_White_House_1993-09-13.jpg/220px-Bill_Clinton%2C_Yitzhak_Rabin%2C_Yasser_Arafat_at_the_White_House_1993-09-13.jpg" width="220" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Bill_Clinton%2C_Yitzhak_Rabin%2C_Yasser_Arafat_at_the_White_House_1993-09-13.jpg/330px-Bill_Clinton%2C_Yitzhak_Rabin%2C_Yasser_Arafat_at_the_White_House_1993-09-13.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Bill_Clinton%2C_Yitzhak_Rabin%2C_Yasser_Arafat_at_the_White_House_1993-09-13.jpg/440px-Bill_Clinton%2C_Yitzhak_Rabin%2C_Yasser_Arafat_at_the_White_House_1993-09-13.jpg 2x" data-file-width="602" data-file-height="411" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bill_Clinton,_Yitzhak_Rabin,_Yasser_Arafat_at_the_White_House_1993-09-13.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Clinton, <a href="/wiki/Yitzhak_Rabin" title="Yitzhak Rabin">Yitzhak Rabin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yasser_Arafat" title="Yasser Arafat">Yasser Arafat</a> during the Oslo Accords on September 13, 1993.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Clinton made a major speech to Congress regarding <a href="/wiki/Clinton_health_care_plan" title="Clinton health care plan" class="mw-redirect">a health care reform plan</a> on September 22, 1993, aimed at achieving universal coverage through a national health care plan. This was one of the most prominent items on Clinton's legislative agenda, and resulted from a task force headed by <a href="/wiki/Hillary_Clinton" title="Hillary Clinton">Hillary Clinton</a>. Though at first well received in political circles, it was eventually doomed by well-organized opposition from conservatives, the <a href="/wiki/American_Medical_Association" title="American Medical Association">American Medical Association</a>, and the health insurance industry. However, <a href="/wiki/John_F._Harris" title="John F. Harris">John F. Harris</a>, a biographer of Clinton's, states the program failed because of a lack of coordination within the <a href="/wiki/White_House" title="White House">White House</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Survivor_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Survivor-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup> Despite the Democratic majority in Congress, the effort to create a national health care system ultimately died when compromise legislation by <a href="/wiki/George_J._Mitchell" title="George J. Mitchell">George J. Mitchell</a> failed to gain a majority of support in August 1994. It was the first major legislative defeat of Clinton's administration.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Natural_33-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Natural-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-The_Survivor_36-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Survivor-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In November 1993, <a href="/wiki/David_Hale_(Whitewater)" title="David Hale (Whitewater)">David Hale</a>, the source of criminal allegations against Bill Clinton in the <a href="/wiki/Whitewater_controversy" title="Whitewater controversy">Whitewater controversy</a>, alleged that Clinton, while governor of Arkansas, pressured him to provide an illegal $300,000 loan to Susan McDougal, the partner of the Clintons in the Whitewater land deal.<sup id="cite_ref-salon031798_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-salon031798-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/U.S._Securities_and_Exchange_Commission" title="U.S. Securities and Exchange Commission">U.S. Securities and Exchange Commission</a> investigation did result in convictions against the McDougals for their role in the Whitewater project, but the Clintons themselves were never charged, and Clinton maintains innocence in the affair.</p>
<p>Clinton signed the <a href="/wiki/Brady_Handgun_Violence_Prevention_Act" title="Brady Handgun Violence Prevention Act">Brady Bill</a> into law on November 30, 1993, which imposed a five-day waiting period on handgun purchases. He also expanded the <a href="/wiki/Earned_Income_Tax_Credit" title="Earned Income Tax Credit" class="mw-redirect">Earned Income Tax Credit</a>, a subsidy for low-income workers.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Survivor_36-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Survivor-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In December of that year, allegations by Arkansas state troopers <a href="/wiki/Larry_Patterson" title="Larry Patterson" class="mw-redirect">Larry Patterson</a> and Roger Perry were first reported by <a href="/wiki/David_Brock" title="David Brock">David Brock</a> in <a href="/wiki/The_American_Spectator" title="The American Spectator">the American Spectator</a>. Later known as <a href="/wiki/Troopergate_(Bill_Clinton)" title="Troopergate (Bill Clinton)">Troopergate</a>, the allegations by these men were that they arranged sexual liaisons for Bill Clinton back when he was governor of Arkansas. The story mentioned a woman named <i>Paula</i>, a reference to <a href="/wiki/Paula_Jones" title="Paula Jones">Paula Jones</a>. Brock later apologized to Clinton, saying the article was politically motivated "bad journalism" and that "the troopers were greedy and had slimy motives."<sup id="cite_ref-apology_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-apology-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<table class="mbox-small" style="border:1px solid #aaa;background-color:#f9f9f9;">
<tr>
<td style="width:1px"></td>

<td colspan="2" class="mbox-text" style="line-height:1.1em"><span><i>Problems playing these files? See <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help">media help</a>.</i></span></td>

<p>That month, Clinton implemented a Department of Defense directive known as "<a href="/wiki/Don%27t_Ask,_Don%27t_Tell" title="Don't Ask, Don't Tell" class="mw-redirect">Don't Ask, Don't Tell</a>", which allowed <a href="/wiki/Homosexuality" title="Homosexuality">gay men and women</a> to serve in the armed services provided they kept their sexuality a secret, and forbade the military from inquiring about an individual's sexual orientation.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup> The policy was developed as a compromise after Clinton's proposal to allow gays to serve openly in the military met staunch opposition from prominent Congressional Republicans and Democrats, including Senators <a href="/wiki/John_McCain" title="John McCain">John McCain</a> (R-AZ) and <a href="/wiki/Sam_Nunn" title="Sam Nunn">Sam Nunn</a> (D-GA). According to <a href="/wiki/David_Mixner" title="David Mixner">David Mixner</a>, Clinton's support for the compromise led to a heated dispute with Vice President Al Gore, who felt that "the President should lift the ban … even though [his executive order] was sure to be overridden by the Congress".<sup id="cite_ref-Mixner2009_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mixner2009-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup> Some gay-rights advocates criticized Clinton for not going far enough and accused him of making his campaign promise to get votes and contributions.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup> Their position was that Clinton should have integrated the military by executive order, noting that President <a href="/wiki/Harry_Truman" title="Harry Truman" class="mw-redirect">Harry Truman</a> used executive order to racially desegregate the armed forces. Clinton's defenders argue that an executive order might have prompted the Senate to write the exclusion of gays into law, potentially making it harder to integrate the military in the future.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Natural_33-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Natural-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup> Later in his presidency, in 1999, Clinton criticized the way the policy was implemented, saying he did not think any serious person could say it was not "out of whack".<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup> The policy remained controversial, and was finally <a href="/wiki/Don%27t_Ask,_Don%27t_Tell_Repeal_Act_of_2010" title="Don't Ask, Don't Tell Repeal Act of 2010">repealed in 2011</a>, removing open sexual preference as a reason for dismissal from the armed forces.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On January 1, 1994, Clinton signed the <a href="/wiki/North_American_Free_Trade_Agreement" title="North American Free Trade Agreement">North American Free Trade Agreement</a> into law.<sup id="cite_ref-NAFTA_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NAFTA-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup> Throughout his first year in office, Clinton consistently supported ratification of the treaty by the U.S. Senate. Clinton and most of his allies in the Democratic Leadership Committee strongly supported free trade measures; there remained, however, strong disagreement within the party. Opposition came chiefly from anti-trade Republicans, protectionist Democrats and supporters of <a href="/wiki/Ross_Perot" title="Ross Perot">Ross Perot</a>. The bill passed the house with 234 votes against 200 opposed (132 Republicans and 102 Democrats voting in favor; 156 Democrats, 43 Republicans, and 1 independent against). The treaty was then ratified by the Senate and signed into law by the President.<sup id="cite_ref-NAFTA_85-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NAFTA-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Violent_Crime_Control_and_Law_Enforcement_Act_of_1994" title="Violent Crime Control and Law Enforcement Act of 1994" class="mw-redirect">Omnibus Crime Bill</a> which Clinton signed into law in 1994<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup> made many changes to U.S. crime and law enforcement legislation including the expansion of the death penalty to include crimes not resulting in death, such as running a large-scale drug enterprise. During Clinton's re-election campaign he said, "My 1994 crime bill expanded the death penalty for drug kingpins, murderers of federal law enforcement officers, and nearly 60 additional categories of violent felons."<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: left; clear: left; margin: 0.5em 1.4em 0.8em 0; width:30em; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #c6dbf7;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>"When I took office, only high energy physicists had ever heard of what is called the Worldwide Web&#160;… Now even my cat has its own page."</p>
</div>
</div>
<div style="text-align: left;"><cite>Bill Clinton's announcement of Next Generation Internet initiative, 1996.<sup id="cite_ref-NetValley_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NetValley-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup></cite></div>
</div>
