<p>The Clinton administration also launched the first official <a href="/wiki/White_House" title="White House">White House</a> website, <a href="/wiki/Whitehouse.gov" title="Whitehouse.gov" class="mw-redirect">whitehouse.gov</a>, on October 21, 1994.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup> It was followed by three more versions, resulting in the final edition launched in 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup> The White House website was part of a wider movement of the Clinton administration toward web-based communication. According to Robert Longley, "Clinton and Gore were responsible for pressing almost all federal agencies, the U.S. court system and the U.S. military onto the Internet, thus opening up America's government to more of America's citizens than ever before. On July 17, 1996, Clinton issued Executive Order 13011&#160;– Federal Information Technology, ordering the heads of all federal agencies to utilize information technology fully to make the information of the agency easily accessible to the public."<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>After two years of Democratic Party control, the Democrats lost control of Congress in the <a href="/wiki/U.S._House_election,_1994" title="U.S. House election, 1994" class="mw-redirect">mid-term elections in 1994</a>, for the first time in forty years.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Clinton_Yeltsin_1995.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Clinton_Yeltsin_1995.jpg/220px-Clinton_Yeltsin_1995.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Clinton_Yeltsin_1995.jpg/330px-Clinton_Yeltsin_1995.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Clinton_Yeltsin_1995.jpg/440px-Clinton_Yeltsin_1995.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="399" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Clinton_Yeltsin_1995.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Clinton and <a href="/wiki/Russian_President" title="Russian President" class="mw-redirect">Russian President</a> <a href="/wiki/Boris_Yeltsin" title="Boris Yeltsin">Boris Yeltsin</a> in October 1995</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Ken_Gormley_(academic)" title="Ken Gormley (academic)">Ken Gormley</a>, Dean of the School of Law at Duquesne University in Pittsburg, authored a book titled <i>The Death of American Virtue: Clinton vs. Starr</i>. In his book, Gormley reveals President Clinton narrowly escaped assassination in the Philippines in 1996. During his visit to the <a href="/wiki/Asia-Pacific_Economic_Cooperation" title="Asia-Pacific Economic Cooperation">Asia-Pacific Economic Cooperation</a> (APEC) forum in Manila, Clinton was saved minutes before his motorcade was scheduled to drive over a bridge charged with a timed improvised explosive device (IED).<sup id="cite_ref-youtube.com_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-youtube.com-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup> According to officials, the IED was large enough to "blow up the entire presidential motorcade".<sup id="cite_ref-Crown_Publishing_Group_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Crown_Publishing_Group-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup> Details of the plot were revealed to Gormley by <a href="/wiki/Lewis_Merletti" title="Lewis Merletti" class="mw-redirect">Lewis Merletti</a>, former member of the Presidential Protection Detail and Director of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secret_Service" title="United States Secret Service">Secret Service</a>. The President was on his way to meet with a senior member of the Philippine government when disaster was averted. Intelligence officers intercepted a radio transmission indicating that there was a wedding cake under a bridge.<sup id="cite_ref-youtube.com_95-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-youtube.com-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup> This alerted Merletti and others as Clinton's motorcade was scheduled to drive over a major bridge in downtown Manila.<sup id="cite_ref-Crown_Publishing_Group_96-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Crown_Publishing_Group-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup> Once more, the word "wedding" was the code name used by a terrorist group for a past assassination attempt.<sup id="cite_ref-Crown_Publishing_Group_96-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Crown_Publishing_Group-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup> Merletti wanted to reroute the motorcade, but the alternate route would add forty-five minutes to the drive time. Clinton was very angry, as he was already late for the meeting; however, following the advice of the secret service saved his life. Two other bombs had been discovered in Manila earlier in the week so the threat level that day was high.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup> Security personnel at the Manila International Airport uncovered several grenades and a timing device in a travel bag.<sup id="cite_ref-Explosives_Found_Near_Summit_Site_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Explosives_Found_Near_Summit_Site-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup> Officials also discovered a bomb near a major U.S. naval base.<sup id="cite_ref-Explosives_Found_Near_Summit_Site_98-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Explosives_Found_Near_Summit_Site-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup> The President was scheduled to visit both of these locations later in the week. An intense investigation took place into the events in Manila and it was discovered that the group behind the bridge bomb was a Saudi terrorist group in Afghanistan known as <a href="/wiki/Al-Qaeda" title="Al-Qaeda">al-Qaeda</a> and the plot was masterminded by <a href="/wiki/Osama_bin_Laden" title="Osama bin Laden">Osama bin Laden</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Crown_Publishing_Group_96-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Crown_Publishing_Group-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup> Until recently, this thwarted assassination attempt was never made public and remained top secret. Only top members of the U.S. intelligence community were aware of these events.<sup id="cite_ref-Crown_Publishing_Group_96-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Crown_Publishing_Group-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Clinton_health_care_elderly.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Clinton_health_care_elderly.jpg/220px-Clinton_health_care_elderly.jpg" width="220" height="151" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Clinton_health_care_elderly.jpg/330px-Clinton_health_care_elderly.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Clinton_health_care_elderly.jpg/440px-Clinton_health_care_elderly.jpg 2x" data-file-width="470" data-file-height="323" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Clinton_health_care_elderly.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Bill Clinton made health care reform one of his highest priorities; the First Lady chaired the Task Force on National Health Care Reform.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/White_House_FBI_files_controversy" title="White House FBI files controversy">White House FBI files controversy</a> of June 1996 arose concerning improper access by the White House to <a href="/wiki/FBI" title="FBI" class="mw-redirect">FBI</a> security-clearance documents. Craig Livingstone, head of the White House Office of Personnel Security, improperly requested, and received from the FBI, background report files without asking permission of the subject individuals; many of these were employees of former Republican administrations.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup> In March 2000, Independent Counsel <a href="/wiki/Robert_Ray_(prosecutor)" title="Robert Ray (prosecutor)">Robert Ray</a> determined that there was no credible evidence of any crime. Ray's report further stated, "there was no substantial and credible evidence that any senior White House official was involved" in seeking the files.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On September 21, 1996, Clinton signed into law the <a href="/wiki/Defense_of_Marriage_Act" title="Defense of Marriage Act">Defense of Marriage Act</a> (DOMA), which defines marriage for federal purposes as the legal union of one man and one woman, allowing individual states to refuse to recognize gay marriages performed in other states.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Paul_Yandura" title="Paul Yandura" class="mw-redirect">Paul Yandura</a>, speaking for the White House gay and lesbian liaison office, said that Clinton's signing of DOMA "was a political decision that they made at the time of a re-election." In defense of his actions, Clinton has said that DOMA was an attempt to "head off an attempt to send a constitutional amendment banning gay marriage to the states", a possibility he described as highly likely in the context of a "very reactionary Congress."<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup> Administration spokesman <a href="/wiki/Richard_Socarides" title="Richard Socarides">Richard Socarides</a> said, "…&#160;the alternatives we knew were going to be far worse, and it was time to move on and get the president re-elected."<sup id="cite_ref-metroweekly_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-metroweekly-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup> Clinton himself stated that DOMA was something "which the Republicans put on the ballot to try to get the base vote for President Bush up, I think it's obvious that something had to be done to try to keep the Republican Congress from presenting that."<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup> Others were more critical. The veteran gay rights and gay marriage activist <a href="/wiki/Evan_Wolfson" title="Evan Wolfson">Evan Wolfson</a> has called these claims "historic revisionism".<sup id="cite_ref-metroweekly_103-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-metroweekly-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup> In a July 2, 2011 editorial <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> opined, "The Defense of Marriage Act was enacted in 1996 as an election-year wedge issue, signed by President Bill Clinton in one of his worst policy moments.".<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup> In June 2013, the United States Supreme Court, in <a href="/wiki/United_States_v._Windsor" title="United States v. Windsor">United States v. Windsor</a>, struck down DOMA.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Despite DOMA, Clinton was the first President to select openly gay persons for Administration positions,<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup> and is generally credited as the first President to publicly champion gay rights.<sup id="cite_ref-newyorker.com_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newyorker.com-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup> During his Presidency, Clinton controversially issued two substantial executive orders on behalf of gay rights, the first lifting the ban on security clearances for LGBT federal employees<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup> and the second outlawing discrimination based on sexual orientation in the federal civilian workforce.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup> Under President Clinton's leadership, federal funding for HIV/AIDS research, prevention and treatment more than doubled.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup> And Clinton also pushed for passing hate crimes laws for gays and for the private sector <a href="/wiki/Employment_Non-Discrimination_Act" title="Employment Non-Discrimination Act">Employment Non-Discrimination Act</a>, which, buoyed by his lobbying, failed to pass the Senate by a single vote in 1996.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup> Advocacy for these issues, paired with the politically unpopular nature of the gay rights movement at the time, led to enthusiastic support for Clinton's election and reelection by the <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Campaign" title="Human Rights Campaign">Human Rights Campaign</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-newyorker.com_108-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newyorker.com-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup> Clinton came out for gay marriage in July 2009<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup> and urged the Supreme Court to overturn DOMA in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup> He was later honored by <a href="/wiki/GLAAD" title="GLAAD">GLAAD</a> for his prior pro-gay stances and his reversal on DOMA.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>As part of a 1996 initiative to curb <a href="/wiki/Illegal_immigration" title="Illegal immigration">illegal immigration</a>, Clinton signed the <a href="/wiki/Illegal_Immigration_Reform_and_Immigrant_Responsibility_Act_of_1996" title="Illegal Immigration Reform and Immigrant Responsibility Act of 1996">Illegal Immigration Reform and Immigrant Responsibility Act</a> (IIRIRA) on September 30, 1996. Appointed by Clinton,<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/History_of_laws_concerning_immigration_and_naturalization_in_the_United_States#1990s" title="History of laws concerning immigration and naturalization in the United States">U.S. Commission on Immigration Reform</a> recommended reducing legal immigration from about 800,000 people a year to about 550,000.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/1996_United_States_campaign_finance_controversy" title="1996 United States campaign finance controversy">1996 United States campaign finance controversy</a> was an alleged effort by the People's Republic of China (PRC) to influence the domestic policies of the United States, before and during the Clinton administration, and involved the fundraising practices of the administration itself. The Chinese government denied all accusations.<sup id="cite_ref-embassy_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-embassy-119"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1996_presidential_election">1996 presidential election</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hillary_Clinton_Bill_Chelsea_on_parade.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Hillary_Clinton_Bill_Chelsea_on_parade.jpg/220px-Hillary_Clinton_Bill_Chelsea_on_parade.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Hillary_Clinton_Bill_Chelsea_on_parade.jpg/330px-Hillary_Clinton_Bill_Chelsea_on_parade.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Hillary_Clinton_Bill_Chelsea_on_parade.jpg/440px-Hillary_Clinton_Bill_Chelsea_on_parade.jpg 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="599" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hillary_Clinton_Bill_Chelsea_on_parade.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
President Bill Clinton (center), first lady Hillary Rodham Clinton (right) and their daughter <a href="/wiki/Chelsea_Clinton" title="Chelsea Clinton">Chelsea</a> (left) wave to watchers at a parade down Pennsylvania Avenue on Inauguration Day, January 20, 1997.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_1996" title="United States presidential election, 1996">1996 presidential election</a>, Clinton was re-elected, receiving 49.2&#160;percent of the popular vote over Republican <a href="/wiki/Bob_Dole" title="Bob Dole">Bob Dole</a> (40.7&#160;percent of the popular vote) and <a href="/wiki/Reform_Party_of_the_United_States_of_America" title="Reform Party of the United States of America">Reform</a> candidate <a href="/wiki/Ross_Perot" title="Ross Perot">Ross Perot</a> (8.4&#160;percent of the popular vote), becoming the first Democratic incumbent since <a href="/wiki/Lyndon_B._Johnson" title="Lyndon B. Johnson">Lyndon Johnson</a> to be elected to a second term and the first Democrat since <a href="/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt" title="Franklin D. Roosevelt">Franklin D. Roosevelt</a> to be elected President more than once.<sup id="cite_ref-Clinton.402_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Clinton.402-120"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup> The Republicans lost a few seats in the House and gained a few in the Senate, but retained control of both houses of the <a href="/wiki/105th_United_States_Congress" title="105th United States Congress">105th United States Congress</a>. Clinton received 379, or over 70&#160;percent of the <a href="/wiki/Electoral_College_(United_States)" title="Electoral College (United States)">Electoral College</a> votes, with Dole receiving 159 electoral votes.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Second_term.2C_1997.E2.80.932001">Second term, 1997–2001</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Clinton1997SOTU.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Clinton1997SOTU.jpg/170px-Clinton1997SOTU.jpg" width="170" height="219" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Clinton1997SOTU.jpg/255px-Clinton1997SOTU.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Clinton1997SOTU.jpg/340px-Clinton1997SOTU.jpg 2x" data-file-width="447" data-file-height="577" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Clinton1997SOTU.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Al_Gore" title="Al Gore">Al Gore</a> and <a href="/wiki/Newt_Gingrich" title="Newt Gingrich">Newt Gingrich</a> applaud as US president Clinton waves during the <a href="/wiki/State_of_the_Union_address" title="State of the Union address" class="mw-redirect">State of the Union address</a> in 1997.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the January 1997 State of the Union address, Clinton proposed a new initiative to provide coverage to up to five million children. Senators <a href="/wiki/Ted_Kennedy" title="Ted Kennedy">Ted Kennedy</a>&#160;– a Democrat&#160;– and <a href="/wiki/Orrin_Hatch" title="Orrin Hatch">Orrin Hatch</a>&#160;– a Republican&#160;– teamed up with Hillary Rodham Clinton and her staff in 1997, and succeeded in passing legislation forming the <a href="/wiki/State_Children%27s_Health_Insurance_Program" title="State Children's Health Insurance Program">State Children's Health Insurance Program</a> (SCHIP), the largest (successful) health care reform in the years of the Clinton Presidency. That year, Hillary Clinton shepherded through Congress the <a href="/wiki/Adoption_and_Safe_Families_Act" title="Adoption and Safe Families Act">Adoption and Safe Families Act</a> and two years later she succeeded in helping pass the <a href="/wiki/Foster_Care_Independence_Act" title="Foster Care Independence Act">Foster Care Independence Act</a>. He negotiated the passage of the <a href="/wiki/Balanced_Budget_Act_of_1997" title="Balanced Budget Act of 1997">Balanced Budget Act of 1997</a> by the Republican Congress. In October 1997, he announced he was getting hearing aids, due to hearing loss attributed to his age, and his time spent as a musician in his youth.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1999 Clinton signed into law the <i>Financial Services Modernization Act</i> also known as the <a href="/wiki/Gramm-Leach-Bliley_Act" title="Gramm-Leach-Bliley Act" class="mw-redirect">Gramm-Leach-Bliley Act</a>, which repealed the part of the <a href="/wiki/Glass%E2%80%93Steagall_Act" title="Glass–Steagall Act" class="mw-redirect">Glass–Steagall Act</a> that had prohibited a bank from offering a full range of <a href="/wiki/Investment_bank" title="Investment bank" class="mw-redirect">investment</a>, <a href="/wiki/Commercial_bank" title="Commercial bank">commercial banking</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Insurance" title="Insurance">insurance</a> services since its enactment in 1933.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Impeachment_and_acquittal">Impeachment and acquittal</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:386px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Senate_in_session.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/43/Senate_in_session.jpg" width="384" height="256" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="384" data-file-height="256" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Senate_in_session.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Clinton's impeachment trial in 1999</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Impeachment_and_acquittal_of_Bill_Clinton" title="Impeachment and acquittal of Bill Clinton">Impeachment and acquittal of Bill Clinton</a></div>
<p>After the 1998 elections, the House <a href="/wiki/Impeachment_of_Bill_Clinton" title="Impeachment of Bill Clinton" class="mw-redirect">impeached Clinton</a>, alleging <a href="/wiki/Perjury" title="Perjury">perjury</a> and <a href="/wiki/Obstruction_of_justice" title="Obstruction of justice">obstruction of justice</a> related to the <a href="/wiki/Lewinsky_scandal" title="Lewinsky scandal">Lewinsky scandal</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Survivor_36-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Survivor-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup> Clinton was only the second U.S. President to be impeached, after <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Johnson" title="Andrew Johnson">Andrew Johnson</a>. Impeachment proceedings were based on allegations that Clinton had illegally lied about and covered up his relationship with 22-year-old White House (and later <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Defense" title="United States Department of Defense">Department of Defense</a>) employee <a href="/wiki/Monica_Lewinsky" title="Monica Lewinsky">Monica Lewinsky</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup> After the <a href="/wiki/Starr_Report" title="Starr Report">Starr Report</a> was submitted to the House providing what it termed "substantial and credible information that President Clinton Committed Acts that May Constitute Grounds for an Impeachment",<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup> the House began impeachment hearings against Clinton before the <a href="/wiki/United_States_midterm_election" title="United States midterm election">mid-term elections</a>. To hold impeachment proceedings, the Republican leadership called a <a href="/wiki/Lame_duck_session_(United_States)" title="Lame duck session (United States)" class="mw-redirect">lame-duck session</a> in December 1998.</p>
<p>While the <a href="/wiki/House_Judiciary_Committee" title="House Judiciary Committee" class="mw-redirect">House Judiciary Committee</a> hearings ended in a straight party-line vote, there was lively debate on the House floor. The two charges passed in the House (largely with Republican support, but with a handful of Democratic votes as well) were for <a href="/wiki/Perjury" title="Perjury">perjury</a> and <a href="/wiki/Obstruction_of_justice" title="Obstruction of justice">obstruction of justice</a>. The perjury charge arose from Clinton's testimony before a <a href="/wiki/Grand_jury" title="Grand jury">grand jury</a> that had been convened to investigate <a href="/wiki/Perjury" title="Perjury">perjury</a> he may have committed in his sworn deposition during <a href="/wiki/Paula_Jones" title="Paula Jones">Paula Jones</a>'s sexual harassment lawsuit.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup> The obstruction charge was based on his actions to conceal his relationship with Lewinsky before and after that deposition.</p>
<p>The Senate later acquitted Clinton on both charges.<sup id="cite_ref-senvoteai_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-senvoteai-126"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup> The Senate refused to meet to hold an impeachment trial before the end of the old term, so the trial was held over until the next Congress. Clinton was represented by Washington law firm <a href="/wiki/Williams_%26_Connolly" title="Williams &amp; Connolly">Williams &amp; Connolly</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup> The Senate finished a twenty-one-day trial on February 12, 1999, with the vote of 55 Not Guilty/45 Guilty on the perjury charge<sup id="cite_ref-senvoteai_126-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-senvoteai-126"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup> and 50 Not Guilty/50 Guilty on the obstruction of justice charge.<sup id="cite_ref-washingtonpostimpeachment_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-washingtonpostimpeachment-128"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup> Both votes fell short of the Constitutional two-thirds majority requirement to convict and remove an officeholder. The final vote was generally along party lines, with no Democrats voting guilty, and only a handful of Republicans voting not guilty.<sup id="cite_ref-senvoteai_126-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-senvoteai-126"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Pardons_and_commutations">Pardons and commutations</span></h4>
<p>Clinton <a href="/wiki/Bill_Clinton_pardon_controversy" title="Bill Clinton pardon controversy">controversially issued</a> 141 pardons and 36 commutations on his last day in office on January 20, 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Survivor_36-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Survivor-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup> Most of the controversy surrounded <a href="/wiki/Marc_Rich" title="Marc Rich">Marc Rich</a> and allegations that Hillary Clinton's brother, <a href="/wiki/Hugh_Rodham" title="Hugh Rodham">Hugh Rodham</a>, accepted payments in return for influencing the president's decision-making regarding the pardons.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup> Some of Clinton's pardons remain a point of controversy.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military_and_foreign_events">Military and foreign events</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_policy_of_the_Bill_Clinton_administration" title="Foreign policy of the Bill Clinton administration">Foreign policy of the Bill Clinton administration</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:President_Clinton_talks_with_Col._Paul_Fletcher,_USAF.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/President_Clinton_talks_with_Col._Paul_Fletcher%2C_USAF.jpeg/220px-President_Clinton_talks_with_Col._Paul_Fletcher%2C_USAF.jpeg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/President_Clinton_talks_with_Col._Paul_Fletcher%2C_USAF.jpeg/330px-President_Clinton_talks_with_Col._Paul_Fletcher%2C_USAF.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/President_Clinton_talks_with_Col._Paul_Fletcher%2C_USAF.jpeg/440px-President_Clinton_talks_with_Col._Paul_Fletcher%2C_USAF.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="1815" data-file-height="1202" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:President_Clinton_talks_with_Col._Paul_Fletcher,_USAF.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
President Clinton speaks with <a href="/wiki/Colonel_(United_States)" title="Colonel (United States)">Col.</a> <a href="/wiki/Paul_J._Fletcher" title="Paul J. Fletcher">Paul Fletcher</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_States_Air_Force" title="United States Air Force">USAF</a>, before boarding <a href="/wiki/Air_Force_One" title="Air Force One">Air Force One</a>, November 4, 1999.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Many military events occurred during Clinton's presidency. The <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Mogadishu_(1993)" title="Battle of Mogadishu (1993)">Battle of Mogadishu</a> occurred in <a href="/wiki/Somalia" title="Somalia">Somalia</a> in 1993. During the operation, <a href="/wiki/MH-60_Black_Hawk" title="MH-60 Black Hawk" class="mw-redirect">two U.S. helicopters</a> were shot down by <a href="/wiki/Rocket-propelled_grenade" title="Rocket-propelled grenade">rocket-propelled grenade</a> attacks to their <a href="/wiki/Tail_rotor" title="Tail rotor">tail rotors</a>, trapping soldiers behind enemy lines. This resulted in an urban battle that killed 18 American soldiers, wounded 73 others, and one was taken prisoner. There were many more Somali casualties. Some of the American bodies were dragged through the streets&#160;– a spectacle broadcast on television news programs. In response, U.S. forces were withdrawn from Somalia and later conflicts were approached with fewer soldiers on the ground. In 1995, U.S. and <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> aircraft <a href="/wiki/1995_NATO_bombing_campaign_in_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="1995 NATO bombing campaign in Bosnia and Herzegovina" class="mw-redirect">attacked Bosnian Serb targets</a> to halt attacks on U.N. safe zones and to pressure them into a peace accord. Clinton deployed U.S. peacekeepers to Bosnia in late 1995, to uphold the subsequent <a href="/wiki/Dayton_Agreement" title="Dayton Agreement">Dayton Agreement</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:President_Clinton_by_Molly_Gilliam,_1999_(DOD_990505-F-7597G-005)_(514619639).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/President_Clinton_by_Molly_Gilliam%2C_1999_%28DOD_990505-F-7597G-005%29_%28514619639%29.jpg/220px-President_Clinton_by_Molly_Gilliam%2C_1999_%28DOD_990505-F-7597G-005%29_%28514619639%29.jpg" width="220" height="154" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/President_Clinton_by_Molly_Gilliam%2C_1999_%28DOD_990505-F-7597G-005%29_%28514619639%29.jpg/330px-President_Clinton_by_Molly_Gilliam%2C_1999_%28DOD_990505-F-7597G-005%29_%28514619639%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/President_Clinton_by_Molly_Gilliam%2C_1999_%28DOD_990505-F-7597G-005%29_%28514619639%29.jpg/440px-President_Clinton_by_Molly_Gilliam%2C_1999_%28DOD_990505-F-7597G-005%29_%28514619639%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1808" data-file-height="1266" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:President_Clinton_by_Molly_Gilliam,_1999_(DOD_990505-F-7597G-005)_(514619639).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
General John P. Jumper, U.S. Air Forces in Europe commander, escorts President William Jefferson Clinton upon his arrival to Ramstein Air Base, Germany, May 5, 1999. The president visited several European air bases to thank the troops (not shown) for their support of NATO Operations Allied Force and Shining Hope, 1999.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In February 1996, the Clinton administration agreed to pay <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a> US$131.8 million in settlement to discontinue a case brought by Iran in 1989 against the U.S. in the <a href="/wiki/International_Court_of_Justice" title="International Court of Justice">International Court of Justice</a> after the shooting down of <a href="/wiki/Iran_Air_Flight_655" title="Iran Air Flight 655">Iran Air Flight 655</a> by the U.S. Navy <a href="/wiki/Guided_missile_cruiser" title="Guided missile cruiser" class="mw-redirect">guided missile cruiser</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Capturing <a href="/wiki/Osama_bin_Laden" title="Osama bin Laden">Osama bin Laden</a> had been an objective of the U.S. government during the presidency of Bill Clinton (and continued to be until <a href="/wiki/Death_of_Osama_bin_Laden" title="Death of Osama bin Laden">bin Laden's death in 2011</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133"><span>[</span>133<span>]</span></a></sup> Despite claims by <a href="/wiki/Mansoor_Ijaz" title="Mansoor Ijaz">Mansoor Ijaz</a> and Sudanese officials that the Sudanese government had offered to arrest and extradite bin Laden and that that U.S. authorities rejected each offer<sup id="cite_ref-articles.latimes.com_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-articles.latimes.com-134"><span>[</span>134<span>]</span></a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/9/11_Commission_Report" title="9/11 Commission Report">9/11 Commission Report</a> stated that "we have not found any reliable evidence to support the Sudanese claim."<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135"><span>[</span>135<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In response to a 1996 State Department warning about bin Laden and the <a href="/wiki/1998_United_States_embassy_bombings" title="1998 United States embassy bombings">1998 bombings of U.S. embassies in East Africa</a> by <a href="/wiki/Al-Qaeda" title="Al-Qaeda">al-Qaeda</a> (which killed 224 people, including 12 Americans), Clinton ordered several military missions to capture or kill bin Laden, both of which were unsuccessful.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136"><span>[</span>136<span>]</span></a></sup> In August 1998, Clinton <a href="/wiki/Cruise_missile_strikes_on_Afghanistan_and_Sudan_(August_1998)" title="Cruise missile strikes on Afghanistan and Sudan (August 1998)">ordered cruise missile strikes on terrorist targets in Afghanistan and Sudan</a>, targeting the <a href="/wiki/Al-Shifa_pharmaceutical_factory" title="Al-Shifa pharmaceutical factory">Al-Shifa pharmaceutical factory</a> in Sudan, which was suspected of assisting bin Laden in making chemical weapons, and bin Laden's terrorist training camps in Afghanistan.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137"><span>[</span>137<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:President_Clinton_greets_the_crowd_at_Spangdahlem_Air_Base.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/President_Clinton_greets_the_crowd_at_Spangdahlem_Air_Base.jpg/220px-President_Clinton_greets_the_crowd_at_Spangdahlem_Air_Base.jpg" width="220" height="156" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/President_Clinton_greets_the_crowd_at_Spangdahlem_Air_Base.jpg/330px-President_Clinton_greets_the_crowd_at_Spangdahlem_Air_Base.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/President_Clinton_greets_the_crowd_at_Spangdahlem_Air_Base.jpg/440px-President_Clinton_greets_the_crowd_at_Spangdahlem_Air_Base.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2100" data-file-height="1486" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:President_Clinton_greets_the_crowd_at_Spangdahlem_Air_Base.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
President Clinton greets Air Force personnel at <a href="/wiki/Spangdahlem_Air_Base" title="Spangdahlem Air Base">Spangdahlem Air Base</a>, May 5, 1999.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>To stop the <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_cleansing" title="Ethnic cleansing">ethnic cleansing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Genocide" title="Genocide">genocide</a><sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138"><span>[</span>138<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139"><span>[</span>139<span>]</span></a></sup> of <a href="/wiki/Albanians" title="Albanians">Albanians</a> by anti-guerilla military units in the former <a href="/wiki/Federal_Republic_of_Yugoslavia" title="Federal Republic of Yugoslavia" class="mw-redirect">Federal Republic of Yugoslavia</a>'s province of <a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Kosovo</a>, Clinton authorized the use of U.S. Armed Forces in a <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> bombing campaign against Yugoslavia in 1999, named <a href="/wiki/Operation_Allied_Force" title="Operation Allied Force" class="mw-redirect">Operation Allied Force</a>. General <a href="/wiki/Wesley_Clark" title="Wesley Clark">Wesley Clark</a> was <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Allied_Commander_Europe" title="Supreme Allied Commander Europe" class="mw-redirect">Supreme Allied Commander of NATO</a> and oversaw the mission. With <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_1244" title="United Nations Security Council Resolution 1244">United Nations Security Council Resolution 1244</a>, the bombing campaign ended on June 10, 1999. The resolution placed Kosovo under UN administration and authorized a <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_Force" title="Kosovo Force">peacekeeping force</a> to be deployed to the region.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140"><span>[</span>140<span>]</span></a></sup> NATO announced that its forces had suffered zero combat deaths,<sup id="cite_ref-roblect_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-roblect-141"><span>[</span>141<span>]</span></a></sup> and two deaths from an <a href="/wiki/Boeing_AH-64_Apache" title="Boeing AH-64 Apache">Apache helicopter</a> crash.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142"><span>[</span>142<span>]</span></a></sup> Opinions in the popular press criticized pre-war genocide statements by the Clinton administration as greatly exaggerated.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143"><span>[</span>143<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144"><span>[</span>144<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2001, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Interim_Administration_Mission_in_Kosovo" title="United Nations Interim Administration Mission in Kosovo">U.N.-supervised</a> <a href="/wiki/Judiciary_of_Kosovo" title="Judiciary of Kosovo">Supreme Court of Kosovo</a> ruled that genocide did not take place, but recognized "a systematic campaign of terror, including murders, rapes, arsons and severe maltreatments."<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145"><span>[</span>145<span>]</span></a></sup> The term "ethnic cleansing" was used as an alternative to "genocide" to denote not just ethnically motivated murder but also displacement, though critics charge there is no difference.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146"><span>[</span>146<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Slobodan_Milo%C5%A1evi%C4%87" title="Slobodan Miloševi?">Slobodan Miloševi?</a>, the president of Yugoslavia at the time of the atrocities, was <a href="/wiki/Trial_of_Slobodan_Milo%C5%A1evi%C4%87" title="Trial of Slobodan Miloševi?">eventually brought to trial</a> before the <a href="/wiki/International_Criminal_Tribunal_for_the_former_Yugoslavia" title="International Criminal Tribunal for the former Yugoslavia">International Criminal Tribunal for the former Yugoslavia</a> in <a href="/wiki/The_Hague" title="The Hague">the Hague</a> on charges of <a href="/wiki/Crimes_against_humanity" title="Crimes against humanity">crimes against humanity</a>, genocide, and war crimes.<sup id="cite_ref-Milosevic_Charges_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Milosevic_Charges-147"><span>[</span>147<span>]</span></a></sup> Miloševi? died in 2006, before the completion of the trial.<sup id="cite_ref-Milosevic_Charges_147-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Milosevic_Charges-147"><span>[</span>147<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148"><span>[</span>148<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In Clinton's <a href="/wiki/1998_State_of_the_Union_Address" title="1998 State of the Union Address">1998 State of the Union Address</a>, he warned Congress that Iraqi dictator <a href="/wiki/Saddam_Hussein" title="Saddam Hussein">Saddam Hussein</a> was possibly pursuing nuclear weapons:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>Together we must also confront the new hazards of <a href="/wiki/Chemical_weapon" title="Chemical weapon">chemical</a> and <a href="/wiki/Biological_weapon" title="Biological weapon" class="mw-redirect">biological weapons</a>, and the outlaw states, terrorists and organized criminals seeking to acquire them. Saddam Hussein has spent the better part of this decade, and much of his nation's wealth, not on providing for the Iraqi people, but on developing nuclear, chemical and biological weapons and the missiles to deliver them. The United Nations weapons inspectors have done a truly remarkable job, finding and destroying more of Iraq's arsenal than was destroyed during the entire gulf war. Now, Saddam Hussein wants to stop them from completing their mission. I know I speak for everyone in this chamber, Republicans and Democrats, when I say to Saddam Hussein, "You cannot defy the will of the world", and when I say to him, "You have used weapons of mass destruction before; we are determined to deny you the capacity to use them again.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149"><span>[</span>149<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Clinton_and_jiang.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Clinton_and_jiang.jpg/220px-Clinton_and_jiang.jpg" width="220" height="158" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/68/Clinton_and_jiang.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/68/Clinton_and_jiang.jpg 2x" data-file-width="250" data-file-height="180" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Clinton_and_jiang.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Bill Clinton and <a href="/wiki/Jiang_Zemin" title="Jiang Zemin">Jiang Zemin</a> holding a joint press conference at the White House, October 29, 1997</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Seeking to weaken Saddam Hussein's grip of power, Clinton signed the <a href="/wiki/Iraq_Liberation_Act_of_1998" title="Iraq Liberation Act of 1998" class="mw-redirect">Iraq Liberation Act of 1998</a> into law on October 31, 1998, which instituted a policy of "regime change" against Iraq, though it explicitly stated it did not provide for direct intervention on the part of American military forces.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150"><span>[</span>150<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151"><span>[</span>151<span>]</span></a></sup> The administration then launched a four-day bombing campaign named <a href="/wiki/Operation_Desert_Fox" title="Operation Desert Fox" class="mw-redirect">Operation Desert Fox</a>, lasting from December 16 to 19, 1998. At the end of this operation Clinton announced that "So long as Saddam remains in power, he will remain a threat to his people, his region, and the world. With our allies, we must pursue a strategy to contain him and to constrain his weapons of mass destruction program, while working toward the day Iraq has a government willing to live at peace with its people and with its neighbors."<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152"><span>[</span>152<span>]</span></a></sup> American and British aircraft in the Iraq no-fly zones attacked hostile Iraqi air defenses 166 times in 1999 and 78 times in 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153"><span>[</span>153<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154"><span>[</span>154<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Clinton's November 2000 visit to <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a> was the first by a U.S. president since the end of the <a href="/wiki/Vietnam_War" title="Vietnam War">Vietnam War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155"><span>[</span>155<span>]</span></a></sup> On October 10, 2000, Clinton signed into law the <a href="/wiki/U.S.%E2%80%93China_Relations_Act_of_2000" title="U.S.–China Relations Act of 2000">U.S.–China Relations Act of 2000</a>, which granted <a href="/wiki/Permanent_normal_trade_relations" title="Permanent normal trade relations">permanent normal trade relations</a> (PNTR) trade status to People's Republic of China.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156"><span>[</span>156<span>]</span></a></sup> The president asserted that free trade would gradually open China to democratic reform.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157"><span>[</span>157<span>]</span></a></sup> Clinton also oversaw a boom of the U.S. economy. Under Clinton, the United States had a projected federal <a href="/wiki/United_States_federal_budget" title="United States federal budget">budget surplus</a> for the first time since 1969.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158"><span>[</span>158<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>After initial successes such as the <a href="/wiki/Oslo_Accords" title="Oslo Accords">Oslo Accords</a> of the early 1990s, Clinton attempted to address the <a href="/wiki/Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_conflict" title="Arab–Israeli conflict">Arab–Israeli conflict</a>. Clinton brought Israeli Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Ehud_Barak" title="Ehud Barak">Ehud Barak</a> and Palestinian Authority Chairman <a href="/wiki/Yasser_Arafat" title="Yasser Arafat">Yasser Arafat</a> together at <a href="/wiki/Camp_David" title="Camp David">Camp David</a> for the <a href="/wiki/2000_Camp_David_Summit" title="2000 Camp David Summit">2000 Camp David Summit</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Survivor_36-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Survivor-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup> Following the peace talk failures, Clinton stated Arafat "missed the opportunity" to facilitate a "just and lasting peace." In his <a href="/wiki/My_Life_(Bill_Clinton_autobiography)" title="My Life (Bill Clinton autobiography)">autobiography</a>, Clinton blames Arafat for the collapse of the summit.<sup id="cite_ref-My_Life_3-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-My_Life-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159"><span>[</span>159<span>]</span></a></sup> The situation broke down completely with the start of the <a href="/wiki/Second_Intifada" title="Second Intifada">Second Intifada</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Survivor_36-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Survivor-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Judicial_appointments">Judicial appointments</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ginsburgandclinton.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Ginsburgandclinton.jpg/220px-Ginsburgandclinton.jpg" width="220" height="143" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Ginsburgandclinton.jpg/330px-Ginsburgandclinton.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Ginsburgandclinton.jpg/440px-Ginsburgandclinton.jpg 2x" data-file-width="450" data-file-height="293" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ginsburgandclinton.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Ruth_Bader_Ginsburg" title="Ruth Bader Ginsburg">Ruth Bader Ginsburg</a> accepting her nomination to the Supreme Court from President Clinton.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Bill_Clinton_Supreme_Court_candidates" title="Bill Clinton Supreme Court candidates">Bill Clinton Supreme Court candidates</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bill_Clinton_judicial_appointments" title="Bill Clinton judicial appointments" class="mw-redirect">Bill Clinton judicial appointments</a></div>
<p>Clinton appointed two justices to the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_United_States" title="Supreme Court of the United States">Supreme Court</a>: <a href="/wiki/Ruth_Bader_Ginsburg" title="Ruth Bader Ginsburg">Ruth Bader Ginsburg</a> in 1993<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160"><span>[</span>160<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Breyer" title="Stephen Breyer">Stephen Breyer</a> in 1994.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161"><span>[</span>161<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Along with his two Supreme Court appointments, Clinton appointed 66 judges to the <a href="/wiki/United_States_courts_of_appeals" title="United States courts of appeals">United States courts of appeals</a> and 305 judges to the <a href="/wiki/United_States_district_courts" title="United States district courts" class="mw-redirect">United States district courts</a>. His 373 judicial appointments are the second most in American history behind those of Ronald Reagan. Clinton also experienced a number of <a href="/wiki/Bill_Clinton_judicial_appointment_controversies" title="Bill Clinton judicial appointment controversies">judicial appointment controversies</a>, as 69 nominees to <a href="/wiki/United_States_federal_judge" title="United States federal judge">federal judgeships</a> did not receive a vote in the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Republican_Party" title="United States Republican Party" class="mw-redirect">Republican</a>-controlled <a href="/wiki/Senate_Judiciary_Committee" title="Senate Judiciary Committee" class="mw-redirect">Senate Judiciary Committee</a>. In all, 84&#160;percent of his nominees were confirmed.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162"><span>[</span>162<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Among the judges appointed by Clinton to the courts of appeals was <a href="/wiki/Sonia_Sotomayor" title="Sonia Sotomayor">Sonia Sotomayor</a>, who was nominated by Clinton in 1997 to the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Court_of_Appeals_for_the_Second_Circuit" title="United States Court of Appeals for the Second Circuit">Second Circuit</a> and confirmed in 1998, following a delay of more than a year caused by Republican opposition.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163"><span>[</span>163<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164"><span>[</span>164<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Clinton was the first president in history to appoint more women and minority judges than white male judges to the federal courts.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165"><span>[</span>165<span>]</span></a></sup> In his eight years in office, 11.6% of Clinton's court of appeals nominees and 17.4% of his district court nominees were black; 32.8% of his court of appeals nominees and 28.5% of his district court nominees were women.<sup id="cite_ref-Scherer.2C_p._85_166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Scherer.2C_p._85-166"><span>[</span>166<span>]</span></a></sup> Clinton appointed the first African American judges to the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Court_of_Appeals_for_the_Fourth_Circuit" title="United States Court of Appeals for the Fourth Circuit">Fourth Circuit</a> (<a href="/wiki/Roger_L._Gregory" title="Roger L. Gregory" class="mw-redirect">Roger L. Gregory</a>) and the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Court_of_Appeals_for_the_Seventh_Circuit" title="United States Court of Appeals for the Seventh Circuit">Seventh Circuit</a> (<a href="/wiki/Ann_C._Williams" title="Ann C. Williams" class="mw-redirect">Ann C. Williams</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-Scherer.2C_p._85_166-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Scherer.2C_p._85-166"><span>[</span>166<span>]</span></a></sup> Clinton also appointed the nation's first openly <a href="/wiki/LGBT" title="LGBT">gay or lesbian</a> federal judge when he named <a href="/wiki/Deborah_A._Batts" title="Deborah A. Batts" class="mw-redirect">Deborah A. Batts</a> to the <a href="/wiki/U.S._District_Court_for_the_Southern_District_of_New_York" title="U.S. District Court for the Southern District of New York" class="mw-redirect">U.S. District Court for the Southern District of New York</a>. Batts was confirmed by the Senate in a <a href="/wiki/Voice_vote" title="Voice vote">voice vote</a> in 1994.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167"><span>[</span>167<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_opinion">Public opinion</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Clinton_approval_rating.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Clinton_approval_rating.png/300px-Clinton_approval_rating.png" width="300" height="190" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Clinton_approval_rating.png/450px-Clinton_approval_rating.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Clinton_approval_rating.png/600px-Clinton_approval_rating.png 2x" data-file-width="834" data-file-height="527" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Clinton_approval_rating.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Clinton's <a href="/wiki/United_States_Presidential_approval_rating" title="United States Presidential approval rating" class="mw-redirect">approval ratings</a> throughout his presidential career</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Clinton's job approval rating fluctuated in the 40s and 50s throughout his first term. In his second term, his rating consistently ranged from the high-50s to the high-60s.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168"><span>[</span>168<span>]</span></a></sup> After his impeachment proceedings in 1998 and 1999, Clinton's rating reached its highest point.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169"><span>[</span>169<span>]</span></a></sup> According to a <a href="/wiki/CBS_News" title="CBS News">CBS News</a>/<i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">New York Times</a></i> poll, Clinton left office with an approval rating of 68&#160;percent, which matched those of <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Reagan" title="Ronald Reagan">Ronald Reagan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt" title="Franklin D. Roosevelt">Franklin D. Roosevelt</a> as the highest ratings for departing presidents in the modern era.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170"><span>[</span>170<span>]</span></a></sup> Clinton's average <a href="/wiki/Gallup_Organization" title="Gallup Organization" class="mw-redirect">Gallup poll</a> approval rating for his last quarter in office was 61%, the highest final quarter rating any president has received for fifty years.<sup id="cite_ref-Jan2001Gallup_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jan2001Gallup-171"><span>[</span>171<span>]</span></a></sup> Forty-seven percent of the respondents identified themselves as being Clinton supporters.<sup id="cite_ref-Jan2001Gallup_171-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jan2001Gallup-171"><span>[</span>171<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>As he was leaving office, a CNN/<i><a href="/wiki/USA_Today" title="USA Today">USA Today</a></i>/Gallup poll revealed that 45&#160;percent of Americans said they would miss him; 55&#160;percent thought he "would have something worthwhile to contribute and should remain active in public life"; 68&#160;percent thought he would be remembered more for his "involvement in personal scandal" than for "his accomplishments"; and 58&#160;percent answered "No" to the question "Do you generally think Bill Clinton is honest and trustworthy?"<sup id="cite_ref-Jan2001Gallup_171-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jan2001Gallup-171"><span>[</span>171<span>]</span></a></sup> The same percentage said he would be remembered as either "outstanding" or "above average" as a president, while 22&#160;percent said he would be remembered as "below average" or "poor."<sup id="cite_ref-Jan2001Gallup_171-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jan2001Gallup-171"><span>[</span>171<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/ABC_News" title="ABC News">ABC News</a> characterized public consensus on Clinton as, "You can't trust him, he's got weak morals and ethics&#160;–  and he's done a heck of a good job."<sup id="cite_ref-langer_172-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-langer-172"><span>[</span>172<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In May 2006, a CNN poll comparing Clinton's job performance with that of his successor, George W. Bush, found that a strong majority of respondents said Clinton outperformed Bush in six different areas questioned.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173"><span>[</span>173<span>]</span></a></sup> Gallup polls in 2007 and 2011 showed that Clinton was regarded by 13% of Americans as the greatest president in U.S. history.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174"><span>[</span>174<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175"><span>[</span>175<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 2014, 18% of respondents in a <a href="/wiki/Quinnipiac_University_Polling_Institute" title="Quinnipiac University Polling Institute">Quinnipiac University Polling Institute</a> poll of American voters regarded Clinton as the best president since World War II, making him the third most popular among postwar presidents, behind <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy" title="John F. Kennedy">John F. Kennedy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Reagan" title="Ronald Reagan">Ronald Reagan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Q_Poll_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Q_Poll-176"><span>[</span>176<span>]</span></a></sup> The same poll showed that just 3% of American voters regarded Clinton as the worst president since World War II.<sup id="cite_ref-Q_Poll_176-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Q_Poll-176"><span>[</span>176<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>A 2015 poll by <i><a href="/wiki/The_Washington_Post" title="The Washington Post">The Washington Post</a></i> asked 162 scholars of the <a href="/wiki/American_Political_Science_Association" title="American Political Science Association">American Political Science Association</a> to rank all the U.S. presidents in order of greatness. According to their findings, Clinton ranked eighth overall, with a rating of 70 percent.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177"><span>[</span>177<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_image">Public image</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Public_image_of_Bill_Clinton" title="Public image of Bill Clinton">Public image of Bill Clinton</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:FEMA_-_14697_-_Photograph_by_Ed_Edahl_taken_on_09-05-2005_in_Texas.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/FEMA_-_14697_-_Photograph_by_Ed_Edahl_taken_on_09-05-2005_in_Texas.jpg/220px-FEMA_-_14697_-_Photograph_by_Ed_Edahl_taken_on_09-05-2005_in_Texas.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/FEMA_-_14697_-_Photograph_by_Ed_Edahl_taken_on_09-05-2005_in_Texas.jpg/330px-FEMA_-_14697_-_Photograph_by_Ed_Edahl_taken_on_09-05-2005_in_Texas.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/FEMA_-_14697_-_Photograph_by_Ed_Edahl_taken_on_09-05-2005_in_Texas.jpg/440px-FEMA_-_14697_-_Photograph_by_Ed_Edahl_taken_on_09-05-2005_in_Texas.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="2000" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:FEMA_-_14697_-_Photograph_by_Ed_Edahl_taken_on_09-05-2005_in_Texas.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Clinton greets a <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Katrina" title="Hurricane Katrina">Hurricane Katrina</a> evacuee, September 5, 2005. In the background holding his jacket is then-Senator <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>As the first <a href="/wiki/Baby_boomer" title="Baby boomer" class="mw-redirect">baby boomer</a> president, Clinton was the first president in more than half a century not to have been alive during World War II.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178"><span>[</span>178<span>]</span></a></sup> Authors Martin Walker and Bob Woodward state Clinton's innovative use of <a href="/wiki/Sound_bite" title="Sound bite">sound bite</a>-ready dialogue, personal charisma, and public perception-oriented campaigning was a major factor in his high public approval ratings.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179"><span>[</span>179<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180"><span>[</span>180<span>]</span></a></sup> When Clinton played the saxophone on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Arsenio_Hall_Show" title="The Arsenio Hall Show">The Arsenio Hall Show</a></i>, he was described by some religious conservatives as "the MTV president."<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181"><span>[</span>181<span>]</span></a></sup> Opponents sometimes referred to him as "Slick Willie", a nickname which was first applied to him in 1980 by <i>Pine Bluff Commercial</i> journalist <a href="/wiki/Paul_Greenberg_(journalist)" title="Paul Greenberg (journalist)">Paul Greenberg</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-mafadgreenberg_182-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mafadgreenberg-182"><span>[</span>182<span>]</span></a></sup> Greenberg believed that Clinton was abandoning the progressive policies of previous Arkansas Governors such as <a href="/wiki/Winthrop_Rockefeller" title="Winthrop Rockefeller">Winthrop Rockefeller</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dale_Bumpers" title="Dale Bumpers">Dale Bumpers</a> and <a href="/wiki/David_Pryor" title="David Pryor">David Pryor</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-mafadgreenberg_182-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mafadgreenberg-182"><span>[</span>182<span>]</span></a></sup> The claim "Slick Willie" would last throughout his presidency.<sup id="cite_ref-WaPoNickname_183-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WaPoNickname-183"><span>[</span>183<span>]</span></a></sup> Standing at a height of <span class="nowrap">6 ft 2 in</span> (1.88&#160;m), Clinton is tied with five others as the <a href="/wiki/Heights_of_presidents_and_presidential_candidates_of_the_United_States" title="Heights of presidents and presidential candidates of the United States">fourth-tallest president</a> in the nation's history.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184"><span>[</span>184<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185"><span>[</span>185<span>]</span></a></sup> His folksy manner led him to be <a href="/wiki/List_of_nicknames_of_United_States_Presidents" title="List of nicknames of United States Presidents">nicknamed</a> <i>Bubba</i>, especially in the <a href="/wiki/Southern_United_States" title="Southern United States">South</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186"><span>[</span>186<span>]</span></a></sup> Since 2000, he has frequently been referred to as "The Big Dog" or "Big Dog."<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187"><span>[</span>187<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188"><span>[</span>188<span>]</span></a></sup> His prominent role in campaigning for <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">President Obama</a> during the <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_2012" title="United States presidential election, 2012">2012 presidential election</a> and his widely-publicized speech at the <a href="/wiki/2012_Democratic_National_Convention" title="2012 Democratic National Convention">2012 Democratic National Convention</a>, where he officially nominated Obama and criticized Republican nominee <a href="/wiki/Mitt_Romney" title="Mitt Romney">Mitt Romney</a> and Republican policies in detail, earned him the nickname "Explainer-in-Chief."<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189"><span>[</span>189<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190"><span>[</span>190<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Clinton drew strong support from the <a href="/wiki/African_American" title="African American">African American</a> community and made improving race relations a major theme of his presidency.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191"><span>[</span>191<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1998, <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize" title="Nobel Prize">Nobel</a> laureate <a href="/wiki/Toni_Morrison" title="Toni Morrison">Toni Morrison</a> called Clinton "the first Black president", saying, "Clinton displays almost every trope of blackness: single-parent household, born poor, working-class, saxophone-playing, <a href="/wiki/McDonald%27s" title="McDonald's">McDonald's</a>-and-junk-food-loving boy from Arkansas".<sup id="cite_ref-MorrisonNewYorker_192-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MorrisonNewYorker-192"><span>[</span>192<span>]</span></a></sup> Noting that Clinton's sex life was scrutinized more than his career accomplishments, Morrison compared this to the stereotyping and <a href="/wiki/Double_standards" title="Double standards" class="mw-redirect">double standards</a> that blacks typically endure.<sup id="cite_ref-MorrisonNewYorker_192-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MorrisonNewYorker-192"><span>[</span>192<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Shortly after he took office, conservative newspaper owner <a href="/wiki/Richard_Mellon_Scaife" title="Richard Mellon Scaife">Richard Mellon Scaife</a> organized a fundraising campaign to smear Clinton's image in the media.<sup id="cite_ref-scaife2_193-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-scaife2-193"><span>[</span>193<span>]</span></a></sup> Leading the <a href="/wiki/Arkansas_Project" title="Arkansas Project">Arkansas Project</a>, Scaife and other associates sought to find sources in Clinton's home state of Arkansas who would be willing to dish out negative allegations against the President.<sup id="cite_ref-scaife2_193-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-scaife2-193"><span>[</span>193<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:ClintonLjubljana.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/ClintonLjubljana.JPG/220px-ClintonLjubljana.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/ClintonLjubljana.JPG/330px-ClintonLjubljana.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/ClintonLjubljana.JPG/440px-ClintonLjubljana.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2560" data-file-height="1920" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:ClintonLjubljana.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Clinton in <a href="/wiki/Ljubljana" title="Ljubljana">Ljubljana</a>, Slovenia, 2009</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1994, <a href="/wiki/Paula_Jones" title="Paula Jones">Paula Jones</a> brought a sexual harassment lawsuit against Clinton, claiming he made unwanted advances in 1991, which he denied. In April 1998, the case was initially dismissed by Judge <a href="/wiki/Susan_Webber_Wright" title="Susan Webber Wright">Susan Webber Wright</a> as lacking legal merit.<sup id="cite_ref-JO.23.24_194-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JO.23.24-194"><span>[</span>194<span>]</span></a></sup> But Jones appealed Webber Wright's ruling, and her suit gained traction following Clinton's admission to having an affair with Monica Lewinsky in August 1998.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195"><span>[</span>195<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1998, lawyers for Paula Jones released court documents contending a pattern of sexual harassment by Clinton when he was governor of Arkansas. <a href="/wiki/Robert_S._Bennett" title="Robert S. Bennett">Robert S. Bennett</a>, Clinton's main lawyer for the case, called the filing "a pack of lies" and "an organized campaign to smear the President of the United States" funded by Clinton's political enemies.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196"><span>[</span>196<span>]</span></a></sup> Clinton later agreed to an out-of-court settlement, paying $850,000.<sup id="cite_ref-CO_197-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CO-197"><span>[</span>197<span>]</span></a></sup> Bennett said that the President only made the settlement so he could end the lawsuit for good and move on with his life.<sup id="cite_ref-clqc_198-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-clqc-198"><span>[</span>198<span>]</span></a></sup> During the deposition for the Jones lawsuit, which was held at the White House,<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199"><span>[</span>199<span>]</span></a></sup> Clinton <a href="/wiki/Lewinsky_scandal" title="Lewinsky scandal">denied having sexual relations</a> with <a href="/wiki/Monica_Lewinsky" title="Monica Lewinsky">Monica Lewinsky</a>&#160;–  a denial that became the basis for an impeachment charge of perjury.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200"><span>[</span>200<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 1992, <a href="/wiki/Gennifer_Flowers" title="Gennifer Flowers">Gennifer Flowers</a> stated that she had a relationship with Clinton that began in 1980.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201"><span>[</span>201<span>]</span></a></sup> Flowers at first denied that she had an affair with Clinton, but later changed her story.<sup id="cite_ref-Flo.2A.5E_202-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Flo.2A.5E-202"><span>[</span>202<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203"><span>[</span>203<span>]</span></a></sup> After Clinton at first denied having a relationship with Flowers on <i>60 Minutes</i>, he later admitted that he had a sexual encounter with Flowers.<sup id="cite_ref-rp.x_204-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rp.x-204"><span>[</span>204<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 1998, <a href="/wiki/Kathleen_Willey" title="Kathleen Willey">Kathleen Willey</a> alleged that Clinton groped her in a hallway in 1993. An independent counsel determined Willey gave "false information" to the FBI, inconsistent with sworn testimony related to the Jones allegation.<sup id="cite_ref-wilo9r_205-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wilo9r-205"><span>[</span>205<span>]</span></a></sup> On March 19, 1998, Julie Hiatt Steele, a friend of Willey, released an <a href="/wiki/Affidavit" title="Affidavit">affidavit</a>, accusing the former White House aide of asking her to lie to corroborate Ms. Willey's account of being sexually groped by President Clinton in the Oval Office.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206"><span>[</span>206<span>]</span></a></sup> An attempt by Kenneth Starr to prosecute Steele for making false statements and obstructing justice ended in a mistrial and Starr declined to seek a retrial after Steele sought an investigation against the former Independent Counsel for prosecutorial misconduct.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207"><span>[</span>207<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Linda_Tripp" title="Linda Tripp">Linda Tripp</a>'s grand jury testimony also differed from Willey's claims regarding inappropriate sexual advances.<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208"><span>[</span>208<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Also in 1998, <a href="/wiki/Juanita_Broaddrick" title="Juanita Broaddrick">Juanita Broaddrick</a> alleged Clinton had raped her though she did not remember the exact date, which may have been 1978.<sup id="cite_ref-CapitalHillBlueWebArchive1_209-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CapitalHillBlueWebArchive1-209"><span>[</span>209<span>]</span></a></sup> In another 1998 event, <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Ward_Gracen" title="Elizabeth Ward Gracen" class="mw-redirect">Elizabeth Ward Gracen</a> recanted a six-year-old denial and stated she had a one-night stand with Clinton in 1982.<sup id="cite_ref-comgrawc_210-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-comgrawc-210"><span>[</span>210<span>]</span></a></sup> Gracen later apologized to Hillary Clinton.<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211"><span>[</span>211<span>]</span></a></sup> Throughout the year, however, Gracen eluded a <a href="/wiki/Subpoena" title="Subpoena">subpoena</a> from Kenneth Starr to testify her claim in court.<sup id="cite_ref-Gracen0s_212-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gracen0s-212"><span>[</span>212<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-presidency_.282001.E2.80.93present.29">Post-presidency (2001–present)</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Post-presidency_of_Bill_Clinton" title="Post-presidency of Bill Clinton">Post-presidency of Bill Clinton</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Photograph_of_President_William_Jefferson_Clinton_Greeting_People_in_a_Large_Crowd_at_a_%22Get_Out_the_Vote%22_Rally_in_Los_Angeles,_California,_11_02_2000.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Photograph_of_President_William_Jefferson_Clinton_Greeting_People_in_a_Large_Crowd_at_a_%22Get_Out_the_Vote%22_Rally_in_Los_Angeles%2C_California%2C_11_02_2000.jpg/220px-Photograph_of_President_William_Jefferson_Clinton_Greeting_People_in_a_Large_Crowd_at_a_%22Get_Out_the_Vote%22_Rally_in_Los_Angeles%2C_California%2C_11_02_2000.jpg" width="220" height="141" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Photograph_of_President_William_Jefferson_Clinton_Greeting_People_in_a_Large_Crowd_at_a_%22Get_Out_the_Vote%22_Rally_in_Los_Angeles%2C_California%2C_11_02_2000.jpg/330px-Photograph_of_President_William_Jefferson_Clinton_Greeting_People_in_a_Large_Crowd_at_a_%22Get_Out_the_Vote%22_Rally_in_Los_Angeles%2C_California%2C_11_02_2000.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Photograph_of_President_William_Jefferson_Clinton_Greeting_People_in_a_Large_Crowd_at_a_%22Get_Out_the_Vote%22_Rally_in_Los_Angeles%2C_California%2C_11_02_2000.jpg/440px-Photograph_of_President_William_Jefferson_Clinton_Greeting_People_in_a_Large_Crowd_at_a_%22Get_Out_the_Vote%22_Rally_in_Los_Angeles%2C_California%2C_11_02_2000.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3150" data-file-height="2026" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Photograph_of_President_William_Jefferson_Clinton_Greeting_People_in_a_Large_Crowd_at_a_%22Get_Out_the_Vote%22_Rally_in_Los_Angeles,_California,_11_02_2000.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Clinton at a Democratic "<a href="/wiki/Get_out_the_vote" title="Get out the vote">Get out the vote</a>" rally in Los Angeles on November 2, 2000</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Bill Clinton continues to be active in public life, giving speeches, fundraising, and founding charitable organizations.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213"><span>[</span>213<span>]</span></a></sup> Clinton has spoken in <a href="/wiki/Prime_time" title="Prime time">prime time</a> at every <a href="/wiki/Democratic_National_Convention" title="Democratic National Convention">Democratic National Convention</a> since 1988.<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214"><span>[</span>214<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Activities_up_until_2008_campaign">Activities up until 2008 campaign</span></h3>
<p>In 2002, Clinton warned that pre-emptive military action against Iraq would have unwelcome consequences,<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215"><span>[</span>215<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216"><span>[</span>216<span>]</span></a></sup> and later claimed to have opposed the Iraq War from the start (though some dispute this).<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217"><span>[</span>217<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2005, Clinton criticized the Bush administration for its handling of emissions control, while speaking at the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Climate_Change_Conference" title="United Nations Climate Change Conference" class="mw-redirect">United Nations Climate Change Conference</a> in Montreal.<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218"><span>[</span>218<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/William_J._Clinton_Presidential_Center_and_Park" title="William J. Clinton Presidential Center and Park" class="mw-redirect">William J.
